The woman [is called] nufasā' (woman in nifas) with ḍamm of nūn and fatḥ of fā' when she gives birth. Legally, it is the blood that exits (subsequent to childbirth) or the exit of most of the child, even if a miscarriage whose some limbs are formed. If it comes out normally, the consideration is its head; if it comes out reversed, by its feet, then the consideration is its navel. What comes after that is nifas. The waiting period ends by its [the child's] delivery, and she becomes umm walad (mother of a child), and he [the husband] commits perjury in his oath by its birth. But he does not inherit nor is prayer performed over him unless most of him came out alive. If she does not see [blood] after it, she is not a nufasā' according to the correct view, and she is obliged only to wuḍū according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). We have previously stated the necessity of ghusl as a precaution according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). Its maximum, i.e., of nifas, is forty days because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not set a time for the nufasā' except forty days unless she sees purity before that. There is no limit for its minimum, i.e., nifas, because there is no need for an additional indicator beyond the birth. And there is no evidence for hayd except its duration of three days, and istihadah is blood less than three days or exceeding [the maximum]... [Then commentary:] His statement: (And nifas) it is named due to the exit of nafs (with sukun of fā', meaning the child) or meaning blood. His statement: (when she gives birth) and also when she menstruates, but the ḍamm is more eloquent for childbirth and the fatḥ for hayd. His statement: (so she is nufasā') with ḍamm of nūn and fatḥ of fā', and with fatḥ of nūn and sukun of fā', and with fatḥ of both. His statement: (it is the blood that exits) this is considering it from the impure substances; as for considering it from the events, it is a legal impediment due to the exit of blood after childbirth from the vagina. His statement: (the exiting) i.e., from the vagina. So if she gave birth from her navel, for example, and blood flows from it, she is not a nufasā' but is a woman with a wound unless it flows from her vagina. However, the other rulings of childbirth apply to the child. His statement: (or the exit of most of the child, and Muhammad and Zafar stipulated the exit of the entire pregnancy. His statement: (even if a miscarriage) with tathlīth of the sīn (three possible vowelizations), meaning the fallen child before completion. His statement: (If it comes out normally) i.e., in the usual manner, by its head. His statement: (and she becomes umm walad) i.e., if the master claims it. His statement: (but he does not inherit) nor is entitled to a bequest, nor does he become free, nor is he named, nor is he washed according to the sunnah. His statement: (she is not a nufasā') and there is no ghusl upon her, and her fasting is not invalidated because they are connected to actual nifas and it did not occur. This is analogy. His statement: (we have stated the necessity of ghusl as a precaution) even if she is not a nufasā', her fasting is invalid. And it was said: rather she is a nufasā' according to him because the child is never devoid of a little blood generally, or because the very exit of the child is nifas. And most mashāyikh follow the statement of Imam, and he also deemed it correct in fatāwā. His statement: (since there is no need for an additional indicator) indicating that it is from the womb because the existence of the child is evidence... His statement: (and there is no evidence for hayd) i.e., there is no evidence indicating that that blood is hayd coming from the womb. Commentary
This passage from Al-Tahtawi's Hashiya defines nifas (postpartum bleeding) and outlines its rulings. Nifas is blood that exits after childbirth or after the majority of the child (even a miscarriage with formed limbs) has exited. If the child comes head-first, the blood after the head emerges counts as nifas; if breech, after the navel emerges. The maximum duration of nifas is 40 days, based on the hadith that the Prophet gave the woman in nifas forty days unless she sees purity earlier. There is no minimum duration; any blood after childbirth is nifas even if only a moment. The text also discusses a difference of opinion: if the woman does not see any blood after delivery, according to the correct view she is not considered in nifas and only needs wudu (according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), but Abu Hanifa held that she should take a ghusl as a precaution. The majority of later scholars (mashāyikh) follow Abu Hanifa's view. The commentary also clarifies that nifas blood must exit from the vagina; if it exits from another place (like a cesarean wound), it is not nifas but considered a wound. The rulings of nifas are similar to hayd in terms of prohibitions (prayer, fasting, etc.) but differ in duration and the start time.

Key Terms
نفاس (nifās): Blood that exits from the vagina after childbirth or after the majority of the child has emerged, considered postpartum bleeding.
نفساء (nufasā'): A woman who is experiencing nifas.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master, thereby becoming free upon her master's death.

Definition and Rulings of Nifas
Defines nifas, conditions for its start, and legal effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of nifas, identify the criterion for its start based on how the child exits, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether blood is necessary.

Core Idea
Nifas legally begins with the majority of the child’s exit, not just the blood; its onset triggers key rulings even without visible bleeding.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi definition of nifas (postnatal bleeding) from the text of al-Tahtawi. You'll learn that the state of nifas begins not merely when blood is seen but when the majority of the child emerges, with specific criteria for head-first or feet-first delivery. This has important consequences for 'idda, umm walad status, oaths, and prayer purity. We will also examine an internal Hanafi disagreement about whether blood must be present for the state of nifas to apply.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the linguistic and legal definitions
Start by noting the linguistic meaning: a woman who gives birth is called nufasa' (with variation in vowelization). Then move to the legal definition: nifas is blood discharged following childbirth OR upon the exit of the majority of the child. Note that the text gives two triggers—blood or child exit—but the latter establishes the state even without blood.
The legal definition focuses on the event of delivery, not solely the presence of blood.
2
Apply the criterion for nifas start based on child’s presentation
If the child descends head-first, nifas begins when the chest exits. If feet-first, it begins when the navel exits. This precision determines the start of the state for rulings like 'idda and umm walad.
The behind (مقعد) is not used; the navel or chest is the marker.
3
Identify the legal effects triggered by nifas
Upon the delivery of the child (majority exit), several rulings take effect: the 'idda (waiting period) ends, the woman becomes an umm walad if she is a slave and the child is acknowledged, and an oath about birth is broken. However, inheritance and the funeral prayer only apply if more than half of the child exits alive.
These effects are tied to the birth event, not necessarily to the presence of nifas blood.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on blood requirement
The text notes a difference: Abu Hanifa requires ghusl as a precaution if no blood is seen, implying she is in nifas. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that without blood she is not in nifas and only needs wudu. The author indicates the correct view (sahih) is the Sahibayn's position, though the precaution is mentioned.
This is an example of ihtiyat (precaution) versus the stronger textual view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
المرأة بضم النون وفتحها إذا ولدت فهي نفساء وشرعاً (وهو الدم الخارج (عقب الولادة) أو خروج أكثر الولد ولو سقطا استبان بعض خلقه فإن نزل مستقيماً فالعبرة بصدره وإن نزل منكوساً . برجليه فالعبرة بسرته فما بعده نفاس وتنقضي بوضعه العدة وتصير أم ولد ويحنث في يمينه بولادته ولكن لا يرث ولا يصلى عليه إلا إذا خرج أكثره حياً وإذا لم ترد ما بعده لا تكون نفساء في الصحيح ولا يلزمها إلا الوضوء عندهما وقدمنا لزوم غسلها احتياطاً عند الإمام
The woman, with damma on the nun and fatha on it, when she gives birth, she is in a state of nifas. Legally, it is blood that emerges following childbirth, or the emergence of more than half of the child, even if it is a miscarriage if some of its limbs are formed. If it descends head-first, then consideration is given to its chest; if it descends feet-first, then consideration is given to its navel; what is after that is nifas. By its delivery, the waiting period ends, she becomes an umm walad, and he breaks his oath by its birth. But he does not inherit, nor is prayer performed over it unless more than half of it comes out alive. And if she does not see anything after it, she is not in nifas according to the correct view, and only wudu is required of her according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and we have presented that ghusl is necessary for her as a precaution according to Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is from Kitab al-Tahara defining nifas (postnatal bleeding). The author begins with the linguistic meaning: a woman who gives birth is called nufasa' (with variations in vowelization). In legal (shar'i) terms, nifas is blood discharged immediately after childbirth (or after the majority of the child emerges). The text specifies that if the child comes out head-first, the criterion is the chest; if feet-first, the criterion is the navel. What exits after that point is considered nifas. This has several legal consequences: the 'idda (waiting period) ends upon delivery, the woman becomes an umm walad (mother of a child) if the master acknowledges the child, and an oath regarding birth is broken. However, inheritance and funeral prayer are not established unless more than half of the child comes out alive. A subtle intra-Hanafi dispute: according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if no blood follows, the woman is not in nifas and only wudu is needed; but Imam Abu Hanifa requires ghusl as a precaution, which the author has mentioned earlier.

Key Terms
نفاس (nifās): Blood discharged after childbirth or after the majority of the child's birth; also the state of a woman in that period.
نفساء (nufasā'): A woman who is experiencing nifas; the term derives from 'nafs' meaning child or blood.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master; upon the child's birth, she becomes free upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Nifas is legally defined by the majority exit of the child (chest or navel criterion), not solely by the presence of blood; the mufta bihi holds that without blood, a woman is not in nifas and only requires wudu.

Maximum and Minimum Duration of Nifas (Postnatal Bleeding)
Ruling on nifas duration with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maximum duration of nifas (40 days) and explain why there is no minimum, citing the Hanafi hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Nifas has a maximum of forty days; any bleeding beyond is istihada.

This lesson explains the temporal boundary of postnatal bleeding (nifas). According to the Hanafi school, nifas lasts up to forty days; there is no defined minimum because childbirth itself is the sign. Bleeding after forty days is considered istihada. This ruling is based on a hadith of the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Nifas has a maximum of 40 days and no minimum. The ruling is a legal limit (had), not a taklifi obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith: 'The Prophet set no time for the woman in nifas except forty days.' (لا وقت للنفساء أربعين يوماً).
This is a ahad hadith, zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The negation of a time except forty indicates that forty is the upper bound; less than forty can be nifas. There is no lower bound because childbirth is the sign.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Shafi'i and others permit up to 60 days based on other reports. Hanafi restricts to 40 days based on the relied-upon hadith.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on this specific hadith; the mufta bihi is 40 days. Bleeding beyond 40 is istihada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأكثره أي النفاس أربعون يوماً لأن النبي لا وقت للنفساء أربعين يوماً إلا أن ترى الطهر قبل ذلك ولا حد لأقله أي النفاس إذ لا حاجة إلى أمارة زائدة على الولادة، ولا دليل للحيض سوى امتداده ثلاثة أيام والإستحاضة دم نقص عن ثلاثة أيام أو زاد على عشرة في الحيض لما رويناه ودم زاد على أربعين في النفاس أو زاد على عادتها وتجاوز أكثر الحيض والنفاس لما قدمناه وأقل الطهر الفاصل بين الحيضتين خمسة عشر يوماً لقوله لأقل الحيض ثلاثة وأكثر عشرة وأقل ما بين الحيضتين خسمة عشر يوماً ولا حد لا كثره لأنه قد يمتد إلى أكثر من سنة إلا لمن بلغت مستحاضة فيقدر حيضها بعشرة وطهرها بخمسة عشر يوماً ونفاسها بأربعين وأما إذا كان لها عادة وتجاوز عادتها حتى زاد على أكثر الحيض والنفاس فإنها تبقى على عادتها والزائد استحاضة وأما إذا نسيت عادتها فهي المحيرة ويحرم بالحيض والنفاس ثمانية أشياء الصلاة والصوم ولا يصحان
And its maximum—i.e., of nifas—is forty days, because the Prophet set no time for the woman in nifas except forty days, unless she sees purity before that. There is no limit for its minimum—i.e., of nifas—since there is no need for an additional sign beyond childbirth. And there is no evidence for hayd except its duration of three days. And istihada is blood that falls short of three days or exceeds ten days in menstruation, according to what we have narrated; and blood that exceeds forty in nifas, or exceeds her habit and surpasses the maximum of hayd and nifas, according to what we have presented. And the minimum purity interval between two menstrual periods is fifteen days, because he said: the minimum of hayd is three, its maximum is ten, and the minimum between two periods is fifteen days. There is no limit for its maximum, because it may extend to more than a year, except for a woman who reaches the age of mustahada: her hayd is estimated as ten, her purity as fifteen days, and her nifas as forty. As for one who has a habit and it exceeds her habit until it exceeds the maximum of hayd and nifas, she remains upon her habit and the excess is istihada. And as for one who forgets her habit, she is the mutahayyira. And eight things are prohibited during hayd and nifas: prayer and fasting, and they are not valid.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage consolidates the temporal boundaries of women's blood-related rulings. Nifas has a maximum of 40 days, based on the hadith that the Prophet gave the woman in nifas a respite of forty days. There is no defined minimum because the childbirth itself is the sign. For hayd (menstruation), there is no prescribed minimum in the Qur'an or hadith, but the Hanafi school uses the 'three days' criterion based on transmitted reports (marwiyyat). Istihada (irregular bleeding) is defined as blood that is less than three days (too short to be hayd) or more than ten days (exceeds the maximum for hayd) or more than forty days for nifas. The purity interval between two periods (tuhr) is at least fifteen days, as deduced from the extremes of hayd (3 and 10). There is no maximum for purity, but a mustahada (woman with prolonged bleeding) is regulated: her hayd is set at ten days, tuhr at fifteen, nifas at forty. If she has a known habit and exceeds it but stays within the maximum, she stays on her habit; the excess is istihada. If she forgets her habit, she is mutahayyira (confused) and must act with caution. The text ends by listing two of the eight prohibitions during hayd/nifas: prayer and fasting are invalid.

Key Terms
استحاضة (istiḥāḍah): Irregular bleeding that falls short of the minimum hayd (3 days) or exceeds the maximum (10 days) or nifas (40 days).
محيرة (muḥayyirah): A woman who has forgotten her habit regarding menstruation; she confuses the mufti and must act with caution.
طهر (ṭuhr): The purity interval between two menstrual periods; minimum is 15 days according to Hanafi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 10 days
B) 15 days
C) 40 days
D) 60 days

Key Takeaway
Nifas has a maximum of 40 days; bleeding beyond is istihada.

Duration of Hayd (Menstruation) and Definition of Istihada
Ruling on hayd duration and istihada definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi limits for hayd (minimum 3, maximum 10 days) and define istihada as bleeding that falls outside those limits.

Core Idea
Hayd is between 3 and 10 days; blood outside this range is istihada.

This lesson focuses on the temporal definition of menstruation (hayd) and irregular bleeding (istihada) in the Hanafi school. Hayd has no prescribed minimum in the Qur'an, but the school sets it at three days based on transmitted reports. The maximum is ten days. Any bleeding less than three days or more than ten days (or exceeding the habit beyond the maximum) is istihada, which does not prevent prayer and fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Hayd has a minimum of 3 days and a maximum of 10 days. These are legal limits (hadood).
2
Define istihada
Istihada is blood that is less than 3 days or more than 10 days (or more than 40 for nifas, or exceeding habit beyond maximum).
3
Locate the dalil for hayd limits
The text says 'لا دليل للحيض سوى امتداده ثلاثة أيام' meaning evidence from marwiyyat (transmitted reports) indicates the three-day minimum and ten-day maximum.
4
Understand the implication for practice
Any bleeding within 3-10 days is hayd; outside that is istihada, which does not prevent prayer and fasting.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
Shafi'i: hayd max 15; Hanafi: 10. This affects when a woman considers herself in hayd vs. istihada.

And its maximum—i.e., of nifas—is forty days, because the Prophet set no time for the woman in nifas except forty days, unless she sees purity before that. There is no limit for its minimum—i.e., of nifas—since there is no need for an additional sign beyond childbirth. And there is no evidence for hayd except its duration of three days. This passage consolidates the temporal boundaries of women's blood-related rulings. Purity Interval (Tuhr) and Rules for Mustahada and Mutahayyira
Ruling on tuhr and rules for mustahada and mutahayyira

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum purity interval (15 days) and explain the rules for a woman with chronic bleeding (mustahada) and one who forgets her habit (mutahayyira).

Core Idea
The purity interval between two periods is at least 15 days; a mustahada is regulated by fixed durations, and a mutahayyira must act with caution.

This lesson covers the minimum purity interval (tuhr) between two menstrual periods, which is 15 days in the Hanafi school. The passage also provides rules for a woman who experiences chronic bleeding (mustahada): her hayd is estimated at 10 days, tuhr at 15, and nifas at 40. For a woman who forgets her habit (mutahayyira), she is considered to be in a state of confusion and must act with extreme caution, treating any doubtful bleeding as hayd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on tuhr
The minimum purity interval between two menstrual periods is 15 days. There is no maximum; it can extend beyond a year.
2
Locate the evidence for tuhr
The text quotes 'he said: the minimum of hayd is three, its maximum is ten, and the minimum between two periods is fifteen days.' This is likely a hadith or report.
3
Explain the deduction
The minimum tuhr of 15 ensures a clear separation between two hayd periods, given the extremes of hayd (3 min, 10 max) so that the sum of min hayd and max hayd (13) is less than 15.
4
Apply to mustahada
A woman who reaches the age of mustahada (chronic bleeder) has her hayd set at 10 days, tuhr at 15, and nifas at 40. She must treat bleeding within these allocated days as hayd/nifas and the rest as istihada.
5
Handle mutahayyira
A woman who forgets her habit is a mutahayyira. She must be cautious: she should consider herself in hayd during any doubt and act accordingly.

The Legal Durations of Hayd, Nifas, and Tuhr
Commentary establishing the legal durations of female blood flows.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the minimum and maximum durations of hayd, nifas, and tuhr, and identify the textual proof for these durations.

Core Idea
Hayd minimum 3 days, maximum 10; nifas maximum 40; tuhr minimum 15 days.

This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi clarifies the foundational durations for female blood flows according to the Hanafi school. The commentator cites a hadith that explicitly establishes these limits, which are essential for determining when a woman is considered pure for worship and marital relations. Understanding these durations is the first step in applying the school's rulings on menstruation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three key durations
Read the text and list the minimum hayd, maximum hayd, maximum nifas, and minimum tuhr. Note that hayd has both a minimum and maximum, nifas only a maximum, and tuhr only a minimum.
The text also states that tuhr has no maximum; it may extend beyond a year.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The text quotes a hadith: 'The minimum of hayd is three, the maximum is ten, and the minimum between two hayd periods is fifteen days.' Identify the type of hadith and its authority.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but the Hanafis accept it due to its clear meaning (qati al-dalala).
3
Analyze the exceptional case of the mustahadah
The text adds a rule for a woman who reaches puberty as a mustahadah (no prior habit). For her, hayd is fixed at ten days, tuhr at fifteen, and nifas at forty.
This is a default ruling when no habitual pattern exists.

سوى امتداده هذه المدة، فاعتبر بالثلاثة أيام لكن تترك الصلاة والصوم بمجرد رؤية الدم، ولو مبتدأة عند أكثر مشايخ بخارى بحر وهو قول أصحابنا قهستاني لأن الأصل الصحة، والحيض دم صحة شمني، وكذا لا يقربها زوجها بالأولى قوله: (والإستحاضة) هي استحيضت المرأة إذا استمر بها الدم واستعماله بالبناء للمجهول لأنه لا اختيار لها في ذلك كجن واغمي كما في الصحاح قوله : دم نقص الخ) هذا على أنها نجس، وأما على أنها حدث فهي حدث بدم الخ ومنها دم الآيسة والحامل والصغيرة أو هو في الصغيرة دم فساد لا استحاضة . قوله : (أو) زاد على عادتها وتجاوز الخ وذلك لأنّ ما رأته على العادة حيض، أو نفاس بيقين، وما جاوز الأكثر استحاضة بيقين، وشككنا فيما بينهما فالحقناه بما جاوز لأكثر لأنه يجانسه من حيث أن كلا منهما مخالف للمعهود فكان الحاقه به أولى إذ الأصل الجري على وفق العادة، ثم قيل تصلي وتصوم في الزائد على العادة لإحتمال أن يجاوز الأكثر فيكون استحاضة وقيل لا لأن الأصل . الصحة هو ودم الحيض دم صحة والاستحاضة دم . علة وأشار الشرح إلى أن هذا هو الصحيح. قوله بين الحيضتين أو بين النفاس والحيض كما في الدر. قوله: (فيقدر حيضها بعشرة من أول ما رأت سواء كان في أول الشهر، أو وسطه أو آخره، وتترك الصلاة بمجرد رؤية الدم على الصحيح هذا قولهما. وقال أبو يوسف، يوقت لها في الصلاة والصوم والرجعة بالأقل وفي الوطء، والتزوج بالأكثر قوله : (فإنها تبقى على عادتها الخ) وتكون هكذا أبدا حتى يزول عنها العارض، أو تموت وهو قول أبي عصمة، وأبي حازم، وقال محمد بن شجاع يقدر حيضها بعشرة وطهرها بعشرين كما لو بلغت مستحاضة، وتنقضي يوماً، وقال الحاكم الشهيد طهرها شهر ان قيل وعليه الفتوى لأنه أيسر على المفتي، والنساء وفي المسئلة أقوال أخر تركنها مخافة الأطناب قوله : (وأما إذا نسيت عادتها فهي المحيرة) بصيغة اسم الفاعل لأنها تحير المفتي، وبصيغة إسم المفعول لأنها حيرت بسبب نسيانها وهي التي كان لها زمن معلوم في وقت معلوم وهي على ثلاثة أوجه إما أن تضل عدد أيامها فقط، أو وقته فقط، أو هما معاً فالكلام عليها في ثلاثة فصول الأول وهو ما إذا نسيت أيام وتعلم إن حيضها في كل شهر مرة فإنها تدع الصلاة ثلاثة أيام من أو الإستمرار لتيقنها

كتاب الطهارة
لفوات شرط الصحة (و) يحرم (قراءة أية من (القرآن إلا بقصد الذكر إذا اشتملت عليه لا على حكم أو خبر، وقال الهندواني : لا أفتي بجوازه على قصد الذكر وإن روي عن أبي
بالحيض فيها، ثم تغتسل سبعة أيام لكل صلاة لتردد حالها فيها بين الحيض، والطهر، والخروج من الحيض، ثم تتوضأ عشرين يوماً لوقت كل صلاة لتيقنها فيها بالطهر، ويأتيها زوجها. الثاني وهو ما إذا ضلت في المكان فإن علمت أن أيامها كانت ثلاثة، ولم تعلم موضعها من الشهر تصلي ثلاثة أيام من أول الشهر بالوضوء للتردد بين الحيض والطهر، ثم تغتسل سبعة وعشرين لكل صلاة لتوهم خروجها من الحيض كل ساعة. الثالث الاضلال بهما أعني العدد والمكان، فالأصل فيه أنها متى تيقنت بالظهر في وقت صلت فيه بالوضوء، وصامت وتوطأ ومتى تيقنت بالحيض تركت ذلك وإن شكت في وقت أنه حيض، أو طهر تحرت فإن لم يكن لها تحرّ صلت فيه بالغسل لكل صلاة لجواز أن يكون وقت الخروج من الحيض، وإن شكت دائماً ولم يكن لها رأي اغتسلت لكل صلاة دائماً على الصحيح، وقيل: لوقت كل صلاة ولا توطأ بالتحري على الأرجح، ولا يحكم لها بشيء من حيض، أو طهر على التعيين، بل تأخذ بالأحوط في حق الأحكام فتصلي الفرائض والواجبات، والسنن المؤكدة لا تطوعاً كالصوم، وتقرأ القدر المفروض، والواجب وتقرأ في الأخيرتين على الراجح لأنها سنة، ولا تدخل مسجداً، ولا تقرأ قرآناً خارج الصلاة ولا تمسه، وتصوم رمضان، ثم تقضي عشرين يوماً إن علمت أن ابتداء حيضها بالليل وإن علمت أنه بالنهار قضت اثنين وعشرين يوماً لأن أكثر ما فسد من صومها أحد عشر يوماً فتقضي ضعف ذلك احتياطاً وإن تعلم شيئاً فعامة المشايخ على العشرين والمفتى به في عدتها التقدير بشهيرين للظهر، وبعشرة أيام للحيض ومن أراد تمام تفاريع صورها وتوضيح أحكامها فعليه بالمطولات فإن ذلك نبذة يسيرة منه . قوله : الصلاة والصوم) اعلم أنهما يمنعان ،وجوبها وجوازها وصحتها ويمنعان صحة الصوم
وجوازه لا وجوبه .
،
قوله : (ولا يصحان لما كان لا يلزم من الحرمة عدم الصحة قال ولا يصحان ولا شك ان المنع من الشيء منع لابعاضه، ولهذا منعاً من سجود التلاوة، والشكر أفاده السيد. قوله : ويحرم قراءة آية من (القرآن) وكذا سائر الكتب المنزلة لأنّ الكل كلام الله تعالى، وكونها منسوخة لا يخرجها عن ذلك الحكم كالآيات المنسوخة من القرآن كذا في الحلبي لكن قال الزيلعي إلا ما بدل منها .
قوله : (إلا) بقصد الذكر ) أي أو الثناء أو الدعاء إن اشتملت عليه فلا بأس به في أصح الروايات. قال في العيون ولو أنه قرأ الفاتحة على سبيل الدعاء أو شيئاً من الآيات التي فيها الدعاء، ولم يرد به ،القرآن فلا بأس به اهـ واختاره الحلواني وذكر في غاية البيان أنه

Book of Purification. (The minimum of hayd is three days and the maximum is ten) based on what we narrated. (And) blood that exceeds forty in nifas, or exceeds her habit and exceeds the maximum of hayd and nifas, as we presented earlier. (And the minimum tuhr separating two hayd periods is fifteen days) because of his statement: the minimum of hayd is three and the maximum is ten, and the minimum between two hayd periods is fifteen days. (And there is no limit to its maximum) because it may extend to more than a year. (Except) for a woman who reaches puberty as a mustahadah (irregular bleeder), her hayd is estimated at ten days, her tuhr at fifteen days, and her nifas at forty days. As for one who has a habit and her habit is exceeded until it exceeds the maximum of hayd and nifas, she remains on her habit and the excess is istihadah. As for one who forgets her habit, she is the muhayyirah (confused woman). (And eight things are prohibited during hayd and nifas: prayer and fasting) and they are not valid. ... (Commentary continues explaining the durations, definitions of istihadah, rules for mustahadah with habit, the three cases of muhayyirah, prohibitions, and exceptions for Quran recitation.)
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya Al-Tahtawi is a commentary on the rulings of menstruation (hayd), postpartum bleeding (nifas), and the period of purity (tuhr). It begins by stating the minimum (three days) and maximum (ten days) of hayd, the maximum of nifas (forty days), and the minimum tuhr between two hayd periods (fifteen days), citing the well-known hadith. The text then addresses the mustahadah—a woman with irregular bleeding—ruling that if she has no prior habit, her hayd is fixed at ten days, tuhr at fifteen, and nifas at forty. If she has a habit that is exceeded, she relies on her habit; the excess is istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding). If she forgets her habit, she becomes a muhayyirah, which is detailed with three cases: forgetting the number of days, the time, or both. The commentary explains the legal reasoning (istihsan, qiyas) and includes intra-Hanafi differences (e.g., Abu Yusuf's distinction between rulings for salah/fasting and intercourse). The passage also lists eight prohibitions during hayd/nifas, focusing on prayer and fasting (which are invalid), and the recitation of Quran (except for dhikr, supplication, or praise). The hashya refines these rulings, noting exceptions for verses of supplication and the opinion of Indianwani on the permissibility of recitation for dhikr. The muhayyirah section outlines precautionary measures for prayer, fasting, and marital relations based on certainty and doubt.

Key Terms
الحيض (al-hayd): Monthly menstrual blood with min 3 days, max 10 days.
النفاس (al-nifas): Postpartum bleeding, max 40 days.
الطهر (al-tuhr): Period of purity between two hayd periods, min 15 days.
المستحاضة (al-mustahadah): Woman with irregular bleeding; if no habit, hayd fixed at 10 days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) 30 days

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school fixed the durations of hayd, nifas, and tuhr based on a prophetic hadith, providing clear legal limits.

Rules for the Mustahadah, Muhayyirah, and Prohibitions during Menses
Commentary on exceptional bleeding and prohibitions during menses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for a mustahadah with a habit, describe the three cases of a muhayyirah, and list the eight prohibited acts during hayd and nifas.

Core Idea
A mustahadah with a habit relies on her habit; the muhayyirah takes precautions; eight acts are prohibited, including prayer and fasting.

This continuation of the passage deals with women whose bleeding deviates from the normal pattern. If a woman has a known habit and bleeds beyond it, she sticks to her habit; the excess is istihadah. If she forgets her habit, she becomes a muhayyirah, requiring a detailed precautionary approach. The text also lists the prohibitions during hayd and nifas, focusing on prayer, fasting, and Quran recitation with important exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish mustahadah with habit vs without
For a woman with a known habit (number of days), if her bleeding exceeds that habit but does not exceed the maximum (10 days for hayd), she remains on her habit. Bleeding beyond the habit but within the maximum is still considered hayd? Actually the text says if it exceeds the maximum, it's istihadah. Wait: The text says 'if she exceeds her habit until it exceeds the maximum of hayd/nifas, she remains on her habit and the excess is istihadah'. This implies that if her habit is, say, 5 days, and she bleeds 8 days (still under 10), that entire 8 days might be hayd? Let me re-read. The passage: 'وأما إذا كان لها عادة وتجاوز عادتها حتى زاد على أكثر الحيض والنفاس فإنها تبقى على عادتها والزائد استحاضة'. So the condition is 'until it exceeds the maximum' meaning if the total bleeding surpasses the maximum (10 days), then she remains on her habit and the extra beyond her habit is istihadah? The phrasing is ambiguous. According to standard Hanafi, if she exceeds her habit but does not exceed 10 days, the whole is hayd. If she exceeds 10 days, she returns to her habit and the extra is istihadah. I need to follow the source. The source says 'إذا كان لها عادة وتجاوز عادتها حتى زاد على أكثر الحيض والنفاس' meaning her habit was within the normal range, then she exceeds that and the total surpasses the maximum. Then she stays on her habit and the excess is istihadah. So the step should clarify: if her habit is known, and she bleeds beyond it but within the maximum, the entire bleeding is hayd? Actually the text doesn't explicitly cover that case. The standard Hanafi position is that if she bleeds beyond her habit but within 10 days, it's all hayd. The text here only addresses when it exceeds the maximum. So for step, I'll note the specific rule mentioned.
The text focuses on the case where bleeding exceeds both habit and maximum. For cases within the maximum, other rules apply.
2
Understand the muhayyirah cases
A woman who forgets her habit becomes a muhayyirah. The text describes three scenarios: (1) forgetting the number of days but knowing the time; (2) forgetting the time but knowing the number; (3) forgetting both. For each, there are specific rulings for prayer, fasting, and marital relations based on precaution.
This is a complex area; the text provides a summary. Full details require consulting larger works.
3
Identify the prohibitions and exceptions
The text lists eight prohibited acts during hayd/nifas, emphasizing prayer and fasting (which are invalid and must be made up for fasting but not prayer). Quran recitation is prohibited except if intending dhikr, supplication, or praise, provided the verse contains those meanings.
The commentary notes that even verses of supplication like 'Rabbana' can be recited with the intention of dua, not tilawah.

Key Terms
المستحاضة (al-mustahadah): Woman with irregular bleeding beyond normal habit or maximum.
المحيرة (al-muhayyirah): Woman who forgets her menstrual habit (number, time, or both).
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Non-menstrual bleeding due to illness or disorder.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
7 min
Mustahad Forgets Number but Knows Time
First scenario: mustahad knows time but forgets number of days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for a mustahad who forgets the number of days of her habit, calculating the periods of ghusl and wudu for each prayer.

Core Idea
When the mustahad forgets the number but knows the time, she starts with ghusl for seven days and ends with wudu for twenty days.

This lesson covers the first scenario of a mustahad who has forgotten her habitual number of menstrual days. She knows the time of the month when her habit typically occurs but cannot recall how many days it lasted. The Hanafi school provides a precise sequence of actions to ensure she maintains ritual purity for prayer without violating the rules of menstruation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the cause of uncertainty
She knows the time but not the count, so she is unsure when she exits menstruation.
2
Identify the period of doubt
She is uncertain for the first seven days (possibly menstruating, possibly pure).
3
Apply ghusl for each prayer in the uncertain period
She performs ghusl (not wudu) for seven days for each prayer due to doubt.
4
Identify the period of certainty
After seven days, she becomes certain of purity for the next twenty days.
5
Apply wudu for each prayer in the certain period
She performs wudu for twenty days, and her husband may approach her.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالحبض فيها، ثم تغتسل سبعة أيام لكل صلاة لتردد حالها فيها بين الحيض والطهر والخروج من الحيض، ثم تتوضأ عشرين يوماً لوقت كل صلاة لتيقنها فيها بالطهر، ويأتيها زوجها. الثاني وهو ما إذا ضلت في المكان فإن علمت أن أيامها كانت ثلاثة ولم تعلم موضعها من الشهر تصلي ثلاثة أيام من أول الشهر بالوضوء للتردد بين الحيض والطهر، ثم تغتسل سبعة وعشرين لكل صلاة لتوهم خروجها من الحيض كل ساعة. الثالث الإضلال بهما أعني العدد والمكان، فالأصل فيه أنها متى تيقنت بالطهر في وقت صلت فيه بالوضوء وصامت وتوطأ ومتى تيقنت بالحيض تركت ذلك وإن شكت في وقت أنه حيض أو طهر تحرت فإن لم يكن لها تحر صلت فيه بالغسل لكل صلاة لجواز أن يكون وقت الخروج من الحيض، وإن شكت دائماً ولم يكن لها رأي اغتسلت لكل صلاة دائماً على الصحيح وقيل لوقت كل صلاة ولا توطأ بالتحري على الأرجح، ولا يحكم لها بشيء من حيض أو طهر على التعيين بل تأخذ بالأحوط في حق الأحكام فتصلي الفرائض والواجبات والسنن المؤكدة لا تطوعاً كالصوم، وتقرأ القدر المفروض والواجب وتقرأ في الأخيرتين على الراجح لأنها سنة، ولا تدخل مسجداً ولا تقرأ قرآناً خارج الصلاة ولا تمسه، وتصوم رمضان ثم تقضي عشرين يوماً إن علمت أن ابتداء حيضها بالليل وإن علمت أنه بالنهار قضت اثنين وعشرين يوماً لأن أكثر ما فسد من صومها أحد عشر يوماً فتقضي ضعف ذلك احتياطاً وإن تعلم شيئاً فعامة المشايخ على العشرين والمفتى به في عدتها التقدير بشهيرين للطهر وبعشرة أيام للحيض
With menstruation in it, then she performs ghusl for seven days for each prayer due to her state bouncing between menstruation, purity, and exiting from menstruation, then she performs wudu for twenty days at the time of each prayer due to her certainty of being in purity, and her husband may have intercourse with her. Second: when she forgets the place [in the month] - if she knows her days were three but does not know their position in the month, she prays three days from the beginning of the month with wudu due to the uncertainty between menstruation and purity, then she performs ghusl for twenty-seven [days] for each prayer due to the possibility of exiting from menstruation every hour. Third: forgetting both, meaning number and place. The principle is: whenever she is certain of purity at a time, she prays at that time with wudu, fasts, and is approached [by husband]; whenever she is certain of menstruation, she abandons that; if she doubts at a time whether it is menstruation or purity, she exercises independent judgment (taharri); if she has no basis for judgment, she prays at that time with ghusl for each prayer because it could be the time of exiting from menstruation. If she doubts constantly and has no opinion, she performs ghusl for each prayer constantly in the soundest view; it is said: at the time of each prayer. She is not approached based on taharri in the most preponderant view. She is not definitively judged to be in menstruation or purity. Rather, she takes the most precautionary in matters of rulings: she prays the obligatory, necessary, and confirmed sunnah prayers, but not supererogatory; she fasts, but not nafl; she recites the obligatory and necessary amount; she recites in the last two rak'ahs according to the preponderant view because it is sunnah; she does not enter a mosque; she does not recite Quran outside of prayer; she does not touch it; she fasts Ramadan, then makes up twenty days if she knows that her menstruation began at night; if she knows it began during the day, she makes up twenty-two days because the maximum of her fast that was spoiled is eleven days, so she makes up double that as a precaution. If she does not know anything, the common practice of the mashayikh is twenty days. The mufta bihi in her waiting period is to estimate two months for purity and ten days for menstruation.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the mustahad (woman with irregular uterine bleeding) who has forgotten her habitual pattern (al-'adah). The author presents three scenarios. First, if she forgets the number of days but knows the time in the month, she must combine caution: she performs ghusl at times of likely transition and wudu when certain of purity. Second, if she forgets the time but knows the number, she prays from the month's start. Third, if she forgets both, she must rely on certainty and precaution, performing ghusl for each prayer when uncertain. In all cases, she observes the normal prohibitions of hayd (prayer, fasting, mosque, Quran) when certain, but resumes acts when certain of purity. The passage emphasizes ihtiyat (precaution) and follows the Hanafi method of resolving doubt through practical rules.

Key Terms
المستحاضة (al-mustahadah): A woman with non-menstrual uterine bleeding (istihadah) that confuses her rulings.
التحري (al-taharri): Exercising personal judgment to determine whether bleeding is hayd or taharah.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Precautionary action taken to avoid violating a ruling when in doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first scenario, how many days does she perform ghusl for each prayer?
A) 10 days
B) 7 days
C) 20 days
D) 27 days

Key Takeaway
When the mustahad knows the time but forgets the number, she performs ghusl for seven days due to doubt, then wudu for twenty days due to certainty.

Mustahad Forgets Time but Knows Number
Second scenario: mustahad knows number but forgets time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for a mustahad who forgets the time of her habit but knows the number of days, calculating the periods of wudu and ghusl.

Core Idea
When the mustahad forgets the time but knows the number, she starts with wudu for three days and then performs ghusl for twenty-seven days.

This lesson presents the second scenario of a mustahad: she knows her menstrual habit lasted three days but does not know which part of the month it occurred. The Hanafi school outlines a procedure of prayer with wudu initially due to uncertainty, followed by ghusl for each prayer for the remaining days to cover the possibility of exiting menstruation at any hour.

Guided Path
1
Identify the known element
She knows the number of days (e.g., three) but not their position in the month.
2
Initial prayer with wudu
She prays three days from the beginning of the month with wudu due to uncertainty between menstruation and purity.
These three days could be her actual menstruation.
3
Subsequent ghusl for remaining days
After the three days, she performs ghusl for each prayer for the next twenty-seven days because she might exit menstruation at any hour.
Twenty-seven days is the remainder of the month (30 - 3).

Mustahad Forgets Both Number and Time
Third scenario: forgetting both number and time, with taharri and ghusl rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for a mustahad who forgets both the number and time of her habit, including the use of taharri and ghusl when uncertain.

Core Idea
When the mustahad forgets both number and time, she relies on certainty and taharri; if uncertain, she performs ghusl for each prayer.

This lesson addresses the most complex scenario: the mustahad has forgotten both the number of days and their position in the month. The Hanafi school establishes a principle: she follows certainty, and in doubt, she exercises personal judgment (taharri) or, lacking that, performs ghusl for each prayer. Constant doubt requires constant ghusl. This scenario emphasizes the concept of precaution (ihtiyat) in worship.

Guided Path
1
Determine certainty of purity or menstruation
If she is certain she is pure at a given time, she prays with wudu, fasts, and can be approached by her husband. If certain she is menstruating, she abandons these acts.
Certainty overrides all other considerations.
2
Handle doubt with taharri
If she doubts whether her bleeding is hayd or taharah, she should exercise independent judgment (taharri) based on available signs (e.g., color, consistency).
Taharri is permissible only if she has a basis for an opinion.
3
No taharri: perform ghusl
If she has no basis for judgment, she prays with ghusl for each prayer because it might be the time of exiting from menstruation.
Ghusl covers all possibilities.
4
Constant doubt: constant ghusl
If she constantly doubts and has no opinion, the soundest view is that she performs ghusl for each prayer constantly (i.e., for every fard prayer).
There is a view that she need only do it at the time of each prayer, but the preferred view is constant ghusl.
5
Marital relations and taharri
The most preponderant view is that she is not approached by her husband based on taharri alone; she must be certain of purity.
Precaution in marital relations.

Source Text

Daily Acts of Worship for the Mustahad
General precautionary rules for daily worship of the mustahad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which acts of worship a mustahad must perform, which she may perform with restrictions, and which are prohibited, based on Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
The mustahad is not definitively judged in hayd or taharah; she takes the most precautionary approach in acts of worship.

This lesson details the practical daily rulings for a mustahad who has forgotten her habit. She is not labeled as menstruating or pure at specific times; rather, she follows precaution (ihtiyat) in all acts of worship. The text specifies what she must pray, fast, recite, and avoid, ensuring she fulfills obligations without committing prohibited acts.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of ihtiyat
She is not definitively judged to be in hayd or taharah; she takes the safest course in rulings.
2
Identify obligatory prayers and fasting
She prays the fard, wajib, and confirmed sunnah (not nafl). She fasts Ramadan but not nafl fasts.
3
Recitation in prayer
She recites the obligatory and necessary portions (al-fatiha and sura). She also recites in the last two rak'ahs because it is sunnah.
There is a difference of opinion, but the preponderant view allows recitation in last two.
4
Prohibitions outside prayer
She may not enter a mosque, recite Quran outside prayer, or touch the mushaf.
These are same as for a menstruating woman.

بالحبض فيها، ثم تغتسل سبعة أيام لكل صلاة لتردد حالها فيها بين الحيض والطهر والخروج من الحيض، ثم تتوضأ عشرين يوماً لوقت كل صلاة لتيقنها فيها بالطهر، ويأتيها زوجها. الثاني وهو ما إذا ضلت في المكان فإن علمت أن أيامها كانت ثلاثة ولم تعلم موضعها من الشهر تصلي ثلاثة أيام من أول الشهر بالوضوء للتردد بين الحيض والطهر، ثم تغتسل سبعة وعشرين لكل صلاة لتوهم خروجها من الحيض كل ساعة. الثالث الإضلال بهما أعني العدد والمكان، فالأصل فيه أنها متى تيقنت بالطهر في وقت صلت فيه بالوضوء وصامت وتوطأ ومتى تيقنت بالحيض تركت ذلك وإن شكت في وقت أنه حيض أو طهر تحرت فإن لم يكن لها تحر صلت فيه بالغسل لكل صلاة لجواز أن يكون وقت الخروج من الحيض، وإن شكت دائماً ولم يكن لها رأي اغتسلت لكل صلاة دائماً على الصحيح وقيل لوقت كل صلاة ولا توطأ بالتحري على الأرجح، ولا يحكم لها بشيء من حيض أو طهر على التعيين بل تأخذ بالأحوط في حق الأحكام فتصلي الفرائض والواجبات والسنن المؤكدة لا تطوعاً كالصوم، وتقرأ القدر المفروض والواجب وتقرأ في الأخيرتين على الراجح لأنها سنة، ولا تدخل مسجداً ولا تقرأ قرآناً خارج الصلاة ولا تمسه، وتصوم رمضان ثم تقضي عشرين يوماً إن علمت أن ابتداء حيضها بالليل وإن علمت أنه بالنهار قضت اثنين وعشرين يوماً لأن أكثر ما فسد من صومها أحد عشر يوماً فتقضي ضعف ذلك احتياطاً وإن تعلم شيئاً فعامة المشايخ على العشرين والمفتى به في عدتها التقدير بشهيرين للطهر وبعشرة أيام للحيض
With menstruation in it, then she performs ghusl for seven days for each prayer due to her state bouncing between menstruation, purity, and exiting from menstruation, then she performs wudu for twenty days at the time of each prayer due to her certainty of being in purity, and her husband may have intercourse with her. Second: when she forgets the place [in the month] - if she knows her days were three but does not know their position in the month, she prays three days from the beginning of the month with wudu due to the uncertainty between menstruation and purity, then she performs ghusl for twenty-seven [days] for each prayer due to the possibility of exiting from menstruation every hour. Third: forgetting both, meaning number and place. The principle is: whenever she is certain of purity at a time, she prays at that time with wudu, fasts, and is approached [by husband]; whenever she is certain of menstruation, she abandons that; if she doubts at a time whether it is menstruation or purity, she exercises independent judgment (taharri); if she has no basis for judgment, she prays at that time with ghusl for each prayer because it could be the time of exiting from menstruation. If she doubts constantly and has no opinion, she performs ghusl for each prayer constantly in the soundest view; it is said: at the time of each prayer. She is not approached based on taharri in the most preponderant view. She is not definitively judged to be in menstruation or purity. Rather, she takes the most precautionary in matters of rulings: she prays the obligatory, necessary, and confirmed sunnah prayers, but not supererogatory; she fasts, but not nafl; she recites the obligatory and necessary amount; she recites in the last two rak'ahs according to the preponderant view because it is sunnah; she does not enter a mosque; she does not recite Quran outside of prayer; she does not touch it; she fasts Ramadan, then makes up twenty days if she knows that her menstruation began at night; if she knows it began during the day, she makes up twenty-two days because the maximum of her fast that was spoiled is eleven days, so she makes up double that as a precaution. If she does not know anything, the common practice of the mashayikh is twenty days. The mufta bihi in her waiting period is to estimate two months for purity and ten days for menstruation.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the mustahad (woman with irregular uterine bleeding) who has forgotten her habitual pattern (al-'adah). The author presents three scenarios. First, if she forgets the number of days but knows the time in the month, she must combine caution: she performs ghusl at times of likely transition and wudu when certain of purity. Second, if she forgets the time but knows the number, she prays from the month's start. Third, if she forgets both, she must rely on certainty and precaution, performing ghusl for each prayer when uncertain. In all cases, she observes the normal prohibitions of hayd (prayer, fasting, mosque, Quran) when certain, but resumes acts when certain of purity. The passage emphasizes ihtiyat (precaution) and follows the Hanafi method of resolving doubt through practical rules.

Key Terms
المستحاضة (al-mustahadah): A woman with non-menstrual uterine bleeding (istihadah) that confuses her rulings.
التحري (al-taharri): Exercising personal judgment to determine whether bleeding is hayd or taharah.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Precautionary action taken to avoid violating a ruling when in doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following prayers is a mustahad permitted to pray?
A) Duha (nafl)
B) Tahajjud (nafl)
C) Fajr sunnah (confirmed sunnah)
D) Witr (wajib)

Key Takeaway
The mustahad follows precaution: she fulfills obligations and confirmed sunnah, but avoids nafl and observes prohibitions of hayd.

Qada of Missed Fasts and Waiting Period for the Mustahad
Rules for making up fasts and calculating iddah for the mustahad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the number of fasts a mustahad must make up and determine her waiting period (iddah) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The mustahad makes up twenty or twenty-two fasts depending on her knowledge, and her iddah is fixed at two months for purity and ten days for menstruation.

This lesson concludes the rulings for the mustahad who has forgotten her habit. The text provides specific instructions for making up missed fasts of Ramadan, using precaution (ihtiyat) by doubling the maximum possible deficient days. It also gives the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling for her waiting period (iddah) should her husband die or divorce occur.

Guided Path
1
Determine the maximum spoiled fasts
The most that could be spoiled from her Ramadan fast is the number of days she was in hayd. The text gives an example: if she knows her menses began at night, she makes up 20 days; if during the day, 22 days.
The basis: 11 is the max possible hayd (max is 10 days of hayd plus first day before hayd? Actually the text says 'أكثر ما فسد من صومها أحد عشر يوماً' meaning max 11 fasts could be invalid due to hayd.
2
Apply the precaution of doubling
She makes up double that maximum (i.e., 22 days) if she knows it began during the day; 20 if at night.
If she has no knowledge, the common practice is 20 days.
3
Apply the mufta bihi for iddah
Her waiting period is estimated at two months for purity and ten days for menstruation.
This is the final ruling for iddah calculation.

Menstruation and the Rulings of Prayer and Fasting
Commentary refining how hayd prevents prayer and fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer and fasting during menstruation and explain why the prohibition invalidates the acts despite the general principle that forbiddance does not imply invalidity.

Core Idea
Menstruation prevents prayer (no obligation) and fasting (obligation remains), and invalidates both acts.

This lesson unpacks a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: how menstruation (hayd) affects prayer and fasting differently. While both are forbidden and invalid during hayd, a woman must make up missed fasts but not missed prayers. The commentary also resolves a logical puzzle: if forbiddance doesn't automatically make an act invalid, why does hayd invalidate prayer and fasting? The answer lies in the nature of the prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and their respective rulings
Read the passage to find what is said about prayer and fasting separately. Note the triple distinction: obligation, permissibility, validity.
Prayer: all three are prevented. Fasting: only permissibility and validity are prevented; obligation remains.
2
Understand the logical objection
The passage raises a principle: 'forbiddance does not necessarily entail invalidity' (la yalzamu min al-hurmati 'adam al-sihhah). Ask: why does the matn say 'they are not valid' if forbiddance alone doesn't imply invalidity?
This sets up the commentator's refinement.
3
Grasp the commentator's refinement
Al-Tahtawi explains that the prohibition here is so comprehensive that it prohibits the parts of the act. Prohibiting the parts renders the act invalid.
He gives the example of prostration of recitation and gratitude, which are also prohibited due to impurity.
4
Apply the refined principle
Use the refined understanding: because hayd prevents the very basis of the act, the act cannot be valid. This is why the matn correctly says 'they are not valid'.
Contrast with other cases where an act is forbidden but still valid, e.g., trade during Friday adhan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : الصلاة والصوم) اعلم أنهما يمنعان وجوبها وجوازها وصحتها ويمنعان صحة الصوم وجوازه لا وجوبه . 
قوله : (ولا يصحان لما كان لا يلزم من الحرمة عدم الصحة قال ولا يصحان ولا شك ان المنع من الشيء منع لابعاضه، ولهذا منعاً من سجود التلاوة، والشكر أفاده السيد.
His statement: 'Prayer and fasting' – know that they prevent its obligation, permissibility, and validity; and they prevent the validity of fasting and its permissibility, not its obligation. His statement: 'And they are not valid' – because forbiddance does not necessarily entail invalidity. He said: And they are not valid, and there is no doubt that prohibition of something is prohibition of its parts, and for this reason they are prohibited from the prostration of recitation and gratitude, as stated by al-Sayyid.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (hashiya) on the matn's ruling that menstruation (hayd) and postnatal bleeding (nifas) prevent prayer and fasting. The commentator clarifies the nuance: for prayer, menstruation prevents its obligation (i.e., no qada), its permissibility (the act is forbidden), and its validity (if attempted, invalid). For fasting, it prevents validity (invalid if done) and permissibility (forbidden), but not the obligation (qada is required). The commentator then refines: why does the matn say 'they are not valid' when forbiddance alone should not imply invalidity? He explains that the prohibition here actually extends to the parts of the act, so it renders the act invalid. This is compared to sajdat al-tilawah and sajdat al-shukr, which are also prohibited due to impurity.

Key Terms
لا يلزم من الحرمة عدم الصحة (la yalzamu min al-hurmati 'adam al-sihhah): A principle: the mere forbiddance of an act does not logically necessitate its invalidity; further evidence is needed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true about fasting during menstruation according to the Hanafi school?
A) Fasting is valid but forbidden
B) Fasting is invalid and no qada is required
C) Fasting is invalid but qada is required
D) Fasting is valid and allowed

Key Takeaway
Menstruation prohibits prayer (no obligation to make up) and fasting (obligation to make up remains), and invalidates both because the prohibition extends to the parts of the acts.

Prohibition of Reciting Quran for Ha'id and Junub
Core prohibition of recitation with proof and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting Quran for ha'id and junub, cite the primary proof, and explain why the prohibition covers even less than a verse.

Core Idea
The ha'id and junub are absolutely prohibited from reciting any part of the Quran, even less than a verse.

This lesson examines the foundational ruling that a menstruating woman (ha'id) and a person in major impurity (junub) are forbidden from reciting the Quran. The primary evidence is a hadith that uses a negation of an indefinite noun, creating generality. The commentator also resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute about reciting less than a verse, affirming absolute prohibition as the chosen view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The text states 'it is prohibited to recite a verse of the Quran' and extends this to 'all other revealed books.' Note that the prohibition applies even to abrogated verses and scriptures.
Al-Zayla'i excepts what has been altered from earlier scriptures.
2
Locate the primary proof
The hadith 'The menstruating woman and the junub should not recite any part of the Quran' is quoted. The commentator explains that 'any part' (شيئاً) is an indefinite noun in a negative context, which indicates generality (umum).
This is supported by a narration from Ali: 'not even one letter.'
3
Analyse the Hanafi dispute on less than a verse
There is disagreement on whether reciting less than a verse is also prohibited. The chosen view (mukhtar) is absolute prohibition, as it falls under the generality of the hadith.
The soundest view prohibits even lesson a verse.
4
Evaluate the exception for dhikr
The base text includes an exception: 'except with the intention of dhikr.' This refers to reciting verses like al-Fatiha as supplication, not as Qur'anic recitation. The soundest narrations allow this.
This is a practical distinction: intention matters.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ويحرم قراءة آية من (القرآن) وكذا سائر الكتب المنزلة لأنّ الكل كلام الله تعالى، وكونها منسوخة لا يخرجها عن ذلك الحكم كالآيات المنسوخة من القرآن كذا في الحلبي لكن قال الزيلعي إلا ما بدل منها . قوله : (إلا) بقصد الذكر ) أي أو الثناء أو الدعاء إن اشتملت عليه فلا بأس به في أصح الروايات. قال في العيون ولو أنه قرأ الفاتحة على سبيل الدعاء أو شيئاً من الآيات التي فيها الدعاء، ولم يرد به القرآن فلا بأس به اهـ واختاره الحلواني وذكر في غاية البيان أنه
معنى
كتاب الطهارة
١٤٣
حنيفة واختلف التصحيح فيما دون الآية وإطلاق المنع هو المختار لقوله : لا تقرأ الحائض ولا الجنب شيئاً من القرآن والنفساء كالحائض (و) يحرم (مسها) أي الآية لقوله تعالى : (لا يمسه إلا المطهرون) سواء كتب على قرطاس أو درهم أو حائط (إلا بغلاف) متجاف عن القرآن والحائل كالخريطة في الصحيح ويكره بالكم تحريماً لتبعيته للابس
المختار كما في البحر والنهر وحيث صحت الرواية عن الإمام فلا يلتفت إلى قول الهندواني لا أفتى بجوازه، وإن روي عن الإمام.
قوله : لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا تقرأ الحائض ولا الجنب شيئاً من القرآن) أي وشيئاً نكرة في سياق النفي فيعم ويؤيده ما أخرجه الدارقطني عن علي رضي الله عنه قال : اقرؤا القرآن ما لم يصب أحدكم جنابة فإذا أصابته فلا ولا حرفاً واحداً والأصح أنه لا بأس بتعليم الحائض والجنب القرآن إذا كان يلقن كلمة كلمة لا على قصد قراءة القرآن كذا في الخلاصة والبزازية أي على قول الكرخي لأنه وإن منع ما دون الآية لكن ما به يسمى قارئاً لا مطلقاً ولهذا قالوا بعدم كراهة التهجي بالقرآن وفي الخانية آخر فصل القراءة تكره قراءة القرآن في مواضع النجاسات كالمغتسل والمخرج والمسلخ وما أشبه ذلك وأما في الحمام إن لم يكن فيه أحد مكشوف العورة وكان الحمام طاهراً فلا بأس بأن يرفع صوته بالقراءة وإن لم يكن كذلك فإن قرأ في نفسه لا يرفع صوته فلا بأس به ولا بأس بالتسبيح والتهليل وإن رفع صوته بذلك، وأما قراءة الماشي، والمحترف إن كان منتبها لا يشغله العمل، والمشي جاز وإلا فلا قال وتكلموا في قراءته مضطجعاً، والأولى أن يقرأ على وجه يكون أقرب إلى التعظيم، ولا بأس بغير القرآن مضطجعاً، والقراءة بالنظر أولى من القراء بالغيب للجمع بين العبادتين. قوله: (ويحرم مسها) أي إلا لضرورة كأن يخاف عليه حرقاً أو غرقاً كما في الحموي عن البرجندي، ويحرم ولو كتب بالفارسية إجماعاً لتعلق جواز الصلاة به للعاجز، وكذا سائر الكتب السماوية كما في القهستاني عن الذخيرة نعم ينبغي أن يخص ما لم يبدل منها، وفيما عدا المصحف إنما يحرم مس الكتابة لا الحواشي، ويحرم الكل في المصحف لأن الكل تبع له كما في الحدادي، وغيره وقيد بالآية لأنه يكره مس ما دونها كما في القهستاني، وفي الخانية من بحث القراءة الحربي، أو الذمي إذا طلب تعلم القرآن والفقه والأحكام يعلم رجاء أن يهتدي لكن يمنع من مس المصحف إلا إذا اغتسل، فلا يمنع بعد ذلك قوله : (إلا) بغلاف متجاف) أي متباعد عنهما . قوله : (كالخريطة) وكالخرج الذي فيه المصحف إذا توسده، أو ركب فوقه في السفر يعني إذا كان ذلك لأجل الحفظ وإلا فيكره كما في الخلاصة. قوله: (وبكره بالكم تحريماً) . صححه في الهداية، وفي المحيط وجامع التمرتاشي لا يكره مسه ، بالكم عند العامة لأن المحرم المس، وذلك بالمباشرة باليد بلا حائل وهما روايتان عن محمد كما في النهاية، قوله: التبعيته للابس) ولهذا لا يجوز له أن يفترشه على نجاسة، ويسجد عليه ولا أن يقوم في مصلاه
His statement: 'And it is prohibited to recite a verse of the Quran' — and likewise all other revealed books, because all are the speech of Allah; being abrogated does not remove them from that ruling, like abrogated verses of the Quran, as in al-Halabi, but al-Zayla'i said except what has been altered. His statement: 'except with the intention of dhikr' — i.e., or praise or supplication if the verse contains it, then there is no harm in the soundest narrations. Al-'Uyun said: If one recites al-Fatihah as a supplication, or some verses containing supplication, not intending it as Quran, there is no harm. Al-Hulwani chose this. It is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan that ... Hanifa differed in correction regarding less than a verse, and absolute prohibition is the chosen view because of his saying: 'The menstruating woman and the junub should not recite any part of the Quran.' And a woman in postnatal bleeding is like the menstruating woman. And it is prohibited to touch it [the verse] because of the Almighty's saying: 'None touch it except the purified.' Whether written on paper, a dirham, or a wall. Except with a covering that is separate from the Quran; a barrier like a pouch is permissible in the soundest view. And it is makruh tahrimi to touch with the sleeve because it follows the wearer. The chosen view is as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr. Where the narration from the Imam is authentic, no attention is paid to the saying of al-Hinduwani: 'I do not give fatwa of its permissibility' even if narrated from the Imam. His statement: 'because of his saying: The menstruating woman and the junub should not recite any part of the Quran' — meaning 'any part' is an indefinite in the context of negation, so it generalizes. This is supported by what al-Daraqutni narrated from Ali: 'Recite the Quran as long as none of you is in janabah; if it happens, then no, not even one letter.' The soundest view is that there is no harm in teaching the menstruating woman and the junub the Quran if they dictate word by word, not intending to recite Quran. This is according to al-Karkhi, because although less than a verse is prohibited, what makes one a reciter is not absolute. Therefore, they said there is no dislike in spelling the Quran. In al-Khaniyah: last chapter of recitation: it is disliked to recite Quran in places of impurity like the bathhouse, toilet, and slaughterhouse. As for the bathhouse if there is no one with exposed awrah and it is pure, then there is no harm in raising one's voice in recitation; otherwise, if he recites to himself without raising his voice, there is no harm. There is no harm in tasbih and tahlil even if one raises his voice. As for recitation while walking or working, if one is attentive and not distracted by work or walking, it is permissible; otherwise no. They discussed recitation while lying down; it is better to recite in a way closer to reverence. There is no harm in reciting other than Quran while lying down. Recitation from sight is better than from memory to combine two acts of worship. His statement: 'And it is prohibited to touch it' — except for necessity such as fear of burning or drowning, as in al-Hamawi from al-Barjandi. And it is prohibited even if written in Persian by consensus, because the permissibility of prayer for the incapable is attached to it. Likewise all heavenly books as in al-Qahistani from al-Dhakhirah. However, it should be specific to what has not been altered. Apart from the mushaf, only the writing is prohibited to touch, not the margins. In the mushaf, all is prohibited because everything is subsidiary to it. It is restricted to the verse because touching less than a verse is disliked. In al-Khaniyah: from the discussion of recitation: a harbi or dhimmi who seeks to learn Quran, fiqh, and rulings may be taught in hope of guidance, but he is prevented from touching the mushaf unless he performs ghusl; then he is not prevented. His statement: 'except with a cover that is separate' — i.e., separate from it [the mushaf and the person]. His statement: 'like a pouch' — and like the bag containing the mushaf if he uses it as a pillow or rides on it in travel, meaning if it is for preservation; otherwise it is disliked. His statement: 'and it is disliked to touch with the sleeve, with prohibition' — this is declared correct in al-Hidayah, while in al-Muhit and Jami' al-Tirmidhi it is not disliked to touch with the sleeve according to the general public because the prohibited is direct contact with the hand without a barrier. These are two narrations from Muhammad. His statement: 'because it follows the wearer' — for this reason, it is not permissible for him to spread it on impurity, prostrate on it, or stand in his prayer area.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is an extensive commentary on the matn's ruling prohibiting the menstruating woman (ha'id) and the one in major impurity (junub) from reciting Quran and touching the mushaf. The commentator first establishes that the prohibition applies to all revealed books, not just the Quran, even abrogated verses, with an exception for altered scriptures according to al-Zaylai. The exception for recitation intended as dhikr or supplication is discussed; the soundest position permits it if one does not intend to recite Quran. The view of al-Hinduwani, who refused to give fatwa on its permissibility, is rejected because the authentic narration from the Imam (Abu Hanifa) supports the exception. The prohibition of touching is based on the Quranic verse 'none touch it except the purified' and applies even if written on coins or walls. A barrier (ghilaf) is required; touching with a sleeve is considered makruh tahrimi. The passage also covers related issues: teaching Quran to a ha'id/junub (allowed if word-by-word), recitation in impure places, recitation while lying down, and the ruling for non-Muslims learning Quran. This showcases the Hanafi method of deriving detailed practical rulings from primary sources.

Key Terms
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, e.g., after sexual intercourse or ejaculation.
النفساء (al-nufasa'): A woman in the postnatal bleeding period; treated like the ha'id in these rulings.
المصحف (al-mushaf): The physical book containing the Quran; touching it is prohibited for those in impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the Hanafi chosen view that reciting less than a verse is prohibited?
A) It is based on consensus
B) The indefinite noun in a negative context indicates generality
C) It is based on analogy with touching
D) It is a concession to avoid hardship

Key Takeaway
The menstruating woman and junub are absolutely prohibited from reciting any part of the Quran, even less than a verse, based on the general evidence of the hadith.

Prohibition of Touching the Mushaf and Exceptions
Prohibition of touching the mushaf with Quranic proof and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why touching the mushaf is haram for ha'id and junub, identify the Quranic proof, and apply the exception for a barrier and necessity.

Core Idea
Touching the mushaf is absolutely prohibited for the impure, based on Quran 56:79; only a separate barrier permits it.

This lesson focuses on the prohibition of touching the mushaf (physical Quran) by a person in impurity. The primary proof is the Quranic verse 'None touch it except the purified.' The commentator explains that this prohibition applies even to writing on coins or walls, and extends to all heavenly books. Exceptions include touching with a separate cover (ghilaf) or in case of necessity. A key intra-Hanafi dispute concerns touching with a sleeve, which is ruled makruh tahrimi in the chosen view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its Quranic proof
The text states 'it is prohibited to touch it [the verse]' and cites Quran 56:79: 'None touch it except the purified.' The pronoun 'hu' refers to the Quran.
This verse is the primary evidence for the prohibition.
2
Determine the scope of the prohibition
The prohibition covers Quranic verses written on any material (paper, coin, wall) and extends to all heavenly books that have not been altered. For the mushaf, even the margins are prohibited because they are subsidiary.
For other books, only the written text is prohibited, not the margins.
3
Examine the exception for a barrier
Touching is allowed if there is a separate covering (ghilaf) that is not attached to the mushaf, like a pouch. The barrier must be distinct from the mushaf.
A sleeve is not considered a valid barrier because it follows the wearer.
4
Analyse the sleeve dispute
There are two narrations from Muhammad: one prohibits touching with the sleeve (makruh tahrimi), the other does not dislike it. The Hidayah declares the first correct, as the sleeve is part of the wearer's garment.
This shows the Hanafi method of settling internal disagreements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ويحرم قراءة آية من (القرآن) وكذا سائر الكتب المنزلة لأنّ الكل كلام الله تعالى، وكونها منسوخة لا يخرجها عن ذلك الحكم كالآيات المنسوخة من القرآن كذا في الحلبي لكن قال الزيلعي إلا ما بدل منها . قوله : (إلا) بقصد الذكر ) أي أو الثناء أو الدعاء إن اشتملت عليه فلا بأس به في أصح الروايات. قال في العيون ولو أنه قرأ الفاتحة على سبيل الدعاء أو شيئاً من الآيات التي فيها الدعاء، ولم يرد به القرآن فلا بأس به اهـ واختاره الحلواني وذكر في غاية البيان أنه
معنى
كتاب الطهارة
١٤٣
حنيفة واختلف التصحيح فيما دون الآية وإطلاق المنع هو المختار لقوله : لا تقرأ الحائض ولا الجنب شيئاً من القرآن والنفساء كالحائض (و) يحرم (مسها) أي الآية لقوله تعالى : (لا يمسه إلا المطهرون) سواء كتب على قرطاس أو درهم أو حائط (إلا بغلاف) متجاف عن القرآن والحائل كالخريطة في الصحيح ويكره بالكم تحريماً لتبعيته للابس
المختار كما في البحر والنهر وحيث صحت الرواية عن الإمام فلا يلتفت إلى قول الهندواني لا أفتى بجوازه، وإن روي عن الإمام.
قوله : لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا تقرأ الحائض ولا الجنب شيئاً من القرآن) أي وشيئاً نكرة في سياق النفي فيعم ويؤيده ما أخرجه الدارقطني عن علي رضي الله عنه قال : اقرؤا القرآن ما لم يصب أحدكم جنابة فإذا أصابته فلا ولا حرفاً واحداً والأصح أنه لا بأس بتعليم الحائض والجنب القرآن إذا كان يلقن كلمة كلمة لا على قصد قراءة القرآن كذا في الخلاصة والبزازية أي على قول الكرخي لأنه وإن منع ما دون الآية لكن ما به يسمى قارئاً لا مطلقاً ولهذا قالوا بعدم كراهة التهجي بالقرآن وفي الخانية آخر فصل القراءة تكره قراءة القرآن في مواضع النجاسات كالمغتسل والمخرج والمسلخ وما أشبه ذلك وأما في الحمام إن لم يكن فيه أحد مكشوف العورة وكان الحمام طاهراً فلا بأس بأن يرفع صوته بالقراءة وإن لم يكن كذلك فإن قرأ في نفسه لا يرفع صوته فلا بأس به ولا بأس بالتسبيح والتهليل وإن رفع صوته بذلك، وأما قراءة الماشي، والمحترف إن كان منتبها لا يشغله العمل، والمشي جاز وإلا فلا قال وتكلموا في قراءته مضطجعاً، والأولى أن يقرأ على وجه يكون أقرب إلى التعظيم، ولا بأس بغير القرآن مضطجعاً، والقراءة بالنظر أولى من القراء بالغيب للجمع بين العبادتين. قوله: (ويحرم مسها) أي إلا لضرورة كأن يخاف عليه حرقاً أو غرقاً كما في الحموي عن البرجندي، ويحرم ولو كتب بالفارسية إجماعاً لتعلق جواز الصلاة به للعاجز، وكذا سائر الكتب السماوية كما في ويسجد عليه ولا أن يقوم في مصلاه

Commentary
This passage is an extensive commentary on the matn's ruling prohibiting the menstruating woman (ha'id) and the one in major impurity (junub) from reciting Quran and touching the mushaf. The commentator first establishes that the prohibition applies to all revealed books, not just the Quran, even abrogated verses, with an exception for altered scriptures according to al-Zaylai. Key Terms
الغلاف (al-ghilaf): A separate cover or pouch for the mushaf that is not attached to it.
المحرم (al-muharram): That which is legally prohibited; here, touching the mushaf is haram.

Additional Permissions and Context for Recitation and Touching
Derivative rulings on teaching, recitation contexts, and non-Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which teaching Quran to a ha'id/junub is allowed, and the rulings for recitation in impure places, while walking or lying down, and for non-Muslims.

Core Idea
The prohibitions are not absolute; teaching word-by-word, reciting in clean places, and reciting as dhikr are permissible contexts.

This lesson covers several derived rulings from the main prohibition: teaching the Quran to a menstruating or junub person is allowed if done word-by-word without the intention of recitation. Recitation in impure places like bathrooms is disliked. Recitation while walking or working is permissible if not distracting. Recitation from sight is better than from memory. Non-Muslims may be taught but prevented from touching the mushaf without purification. These rulings show the nuance of Hanafi fiqh in applying principles to various contexts.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling on teaching
It is permissible to teach a ha'id or junub if the teacher dictates word by word, not intending to recite Quran. This is based on al-Karkhi's view that what makes one a 'reciter' is not absolute.
This allows educational contexts without sin.
2
Identify the ruling on recitation in impure places
Reciting Quran in places of impurity (bathhouse, toilet, slaughterhouse) is disliked. If the place is pure and no awrah is exposed, raising the voice is permissible; otherwise, silent recitation is allowed.
The principle of reverence (ta'dhim) governs this.
3
Examine recitation while walking or working
If the person is attentive and not distracted by work or walking, recitation is permissible; otherwise it is not. Similarly, recitation while lying down is allowed but it is better to be in a reverent posture.
The condition is mental presence, not physical posture.
4
Analyse the ruling for non-Muslims
A harbi or dhimmi may be taught Quran and fiqh in hope of guidance, but they are prevented from touching the mushaf unless they perform ghusl. After ghusl, they are not prevented.
This shows the priority of da'wah over prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
