معنى
كتاب الطهارة
١٤٣
حنيفة واختلف التصحيح فيما دون الآية وإطلاق المنع هو المختار لقوله : لا تقرأ الحائض ولا الجنب شيئاً من القرآن والنفساء كالحائض (و) يحرم (مسها) أي الآية لقوله تعالى : (لا يمسه إلا المطهرون) سواء كتب على قرطاس أو درهم أو حائط (إلا بغلاف) متجاف عن القرآن والحائل كالخريطة في الصحيح ويكره بالكم تحريماً لتبعيته للابس
المختار كما في البحر والنهر وحيث صحت الرواية عن الإمام فلا يلتفت إلى قول الهندواني لا أفتى بجوازه، وإن روي عن الإمام.
قوله : لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا تقرأ الحائض ولا الجنب شيئاً من القرآن) أي وشيئاً نكرة في سياق النفي فيعم ويؤيده ما أخرجه الدارقطني عن علي رضي الله عنه قال : اقرؤا القرآن ما لم يصب أحدكم جنابة فإذا أصابته فلا ولا حرفاً واحداً والأصح أنه لا بأس بتعليم الحائض والجنب القرآن إذا كان يلقن كلمة كلمة لا على قصد قراءة القرآن كذا في الخلاصة والبزازية أي على قول الكرخي لأنه وإن منع ما دون الآية لكن ما به يسمى قارئاً لا مطلقاً ولهذا قالوا بعدم كراهة التهجي بالقرآن وفي الخانية آخر فصل القراءة تكره قراءة القرآن في مواضع النجاسات كالمغتسل والمخرج والمسلخ وما أشبه ذلك وأما في الحمام إن لم يكن فيه أحد مكشوف العورة وكان الحمام طاهراً فلا بأس بأن يرفع صوته بالقراءة وإن لم يكن كذلك فإن قرأ في نفسه لا يرفع صوته فلا بأس به ولا بأس بالتسبيح والتهليل وإن رفع صوته بذلك، وأما قراءة الماشي، والمحترف إن كان منتبها لا يشغله العمل، والمشي جاز وإلا فلا قال وتكلموا في قراءته مضطجعاً، والأولى أن يقرأ على وجه يكون أقرب إلى التعظيم، ولا بأس بغير القرآن مضطجعاً، والقراءة بالنظر أولى من القراء بالغيب للجمع بين العبادتين. قوله: (ويحرم مسها) أي إلا لضرورة كأن يخاف عليه حرقاً أو غرقاً كما في الحموي عن البرجندي، ويحرم ولو كتب بالفارسية إجماعاً لتعلق جواز الصلاة به للعاجز، وكذا سائر الكتب السماوية كما في القهستاني عن الذخيرة نعم ينبغي أن يخص ما لم يبدل منها، وفيما عدا المصحف إنما يحرم مس الكتابة لا الحواشي، ويحرم الكل في المصحف لأن الكل تبع له كما في الحدادي، وغيره وقيد بالآية لأنه يكره مس ما دونها كما في القهستاني، وفي الخانية من بحث القراءة الحربي، أو الذمي إذا طلب تعلم القرآن والفقه والأحكام يعلم رجاء أن يهتدي لكن يمنع من مس المصحف إلا إذا اغتسل، فلا يمنع بعد ذلك قوله : (إلا) بغلاف متجاف) أي متباعد عنهما . قوله : (كالخريطة) وكالخرج الذي فيه المصحف إذا توسده، أو ركب فوقه في السفر يعني إذا كان ذلك لأجل الحفظ وإلا فيكره كما في الخلاصة. قوله: (وبكره بالكم تحريماً) . صححه في الهداية، وفي المحيط وجامع التمرتاشي لا يكره مسه ، بالكم عند العامة لأن المحرم المس، وذلك بالمباشرة باليد بلا حائل وهما روايتان عن محمد كما في النهاية، قوله: التبعيته للابس) ولهذا لا يجوز له أن يفترشه على نجاسة، ويسجد عليه ولا أن يقوم في مصلاه
His statement: 'And it is prohibited to recite a verse of the Quran' — and likewise all other revealed books, because all are the speech of Allah; being abrogated does not remove them from that ruling, like abrogated verses of the Quran, as in al-Halabi, but al-Zayla'i said except what has been altered. His statement: 'except with the intention of dhikr' — i.e., or praise or supplication if the verse contains it, then there is no harm in the soundest narrations. Al-'Uyun said: If one recites al-Fatihah as a supplication, or some verses containing supplication, not intending it as Quran, there is no harm. Al-Hulwani chose this. It is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan that ... Hanifa differed in correction regarding less than a verse, and absolute prohibition is the chosen view because of his saying: 'The menstruating woman and the junub should not recite any part of the Quran.' And a woman in postnatal bleeding is like the menstruating woman. And it is prohibited to touch it [the verse] because of the Almighty's saying: 'None touch it except the purified.' Whether written on paper, a dirham, or a wall. Except with a covering that is separate from the Quran; a barrier like a pouch is permissible in the soundest view. And it is makruh tahrimi to touch with the sleeve because it follows the wearer. The chosen view is as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr. Where the narration from the Imam is authentic, no attention is paid to the saying of al-Hinduwani: 'I do not give fatwa of its permissibility' even if narrated from the Imam. His statement: 'because of his saying: The menstruating woman and the junub should not recite any part of the Quran' — meaning 'any part' is an indefinite in the context of negation, so it generalizes. This is supported by what al-Daraqutni narrated from Ali: 'Recite the Quran as long as none of you is in janabah; if it happens, then no, not even one letter.' The soundest view is that there is no harm in teaching the menstruating woman and the junub the Quran if they dictate word by word, not intending to recite Quran. This is according to al-Karkhi, because although less than a verse is prohibited, what makes one a reciter is not absolute. Therefore, they said there is no dislike in spelling the Quran. In al-Khaniyah: last chapter of recitation: it is disliked to recite Quran in places of impurity like the bathhouse, toilet, and slaughterhouse. As for the bathhouse if there is no one with exposed awrah and it is pure, then there is no harm in raising one's voice in recitation; otherwise, if he recites to himself without raising his voice, there is no harm. There is no harm in tasbih and tahlil even if one raises his voice. As for recitation while walking or working, if one is attentive and not distracted by work or walking, it is permissible; otherwise no. They discussed recitation while lying down; it is better to recite in a way closer to reverence. There is no harm in reciting other than Quran while lying down. Recitation from sight is better than from memory to combine two acts of worship. His statement: 'And it is prohibited to touch it' — except for necessity such as fear of burning or drowning, as in al-Hamawi from al-Barjandi. And it is prohibited even if written in Persian by consensus, because the permissibility of prayer for the incapable is attached to it. Likewise all heavenly books as in al-Qahistani from al-Dhakhirah. However, it should be specific to what has not been altered. Apart from the mushaf, only the writing is prohibited to touch, not the margins. In the mushaf, all is prohibited because everything is subsidiary to it. It is restricted to the verse because touching less than a verse is disliked. In al-Khaniyah: from the discussion of recitation: a harbi or dhimmi who seeks to learn Quran, fiqh, and rulings may be taught in hope of guidance, but he is prevented from touching the mushaf unless he performs ghusl; then he is not prevented. His statement: 'except with a cover that is separate' — i.e., separate from it [the mushaf and the person]. His statement: 'like a pouch' — and like the bag containing the mushaf if he uses it as a pillow or rides on it in travel, meaning if it is for preservation; otherwise it is disliked. His statement: 'and it is disliked to touch with the sleeve, with prohibition' — this is declared correct in al-Hidayah, while in al-Muhit and Jami' al-Tirmidhi it is not disliked to touch with the sleeve according to the general public because the prohibited is direct contact with the hand without a barrier. These are two narrations from Muhammad. His statement: 'because it follows the wearer' — for this reason, it is not permissible for him to spread it on impurity, prostrate on it, or stand in his prayer area.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is an extensive commentary on the matn's ruling prohibiting the menstruating woman (ha'id) and the one in major impurity (junub) from reciting Quran and touching the mushaf. The commentator first establishes that the prohibition applies to all revealed books, not just the Quran, even abrogated verses, with an exception for altered scriptures according to al-Zaylai. The exception for recitation intended as dhikr or supplication is discussed; the soundest position permits it if one does not intend to recite Quran. The view of al-Hinduwani, who refused to give fatwa on its permissibility, is rejected because the authentic narration from the Imam (Abu Hanifa) supports the exception. The prohibition of touching is based on the Quranic verse 'none touch it except the purified' and applies even if written on coins or walls. A barrier (ghilaf) is required; touching with a sleeve is considered makruh tahrimi. The passage also covers related issues: teaching Quran to a ha'id/junub (allowed if word-by-word), recitation in impure places, recitation while lying down, and the ruling for non-Muslims learning Quran. This showcases the Hanafi method of deriving detailed practical rulings from primary sources.

Key Terms
التهجي (al-tahajji): Spelling out the letters of the Quran without reciting as a continuous text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on reciting Quran in a clean bathhouse where no one is exposed?
A) Prohibited
B) Disliked
C) Permissible to raise voice
D) Permissible only silently

Key Takeaway
Numerous contexts permit recitation or teaching despite the general prohibition, demonstrating the flexibility of Hanafi fiqh.

Taharah — Purification

Prohibition of Quran Recitation for Ha’id and Junub: Proof and Application
Ruling with textual proof and an intra-Hanafi refinement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Quran recitation for a menstruating woman and a person in janabah, explain the proof from hadith, and distinguish the permissible exception of teaching word by word.

Core Idea
A menstruating woman and a junub are absolutely prohibited from reciting any part of the Quran, even a single letter.

In this lesson, we examine a fundamental ruling from the chapter of Taharah: the prohibition of Quran recitation for a menstruating woman (ha'id) and a person in a state of major ritual impurity (junub). This ruling is based on a prophetic hadith and is supported by the practice of the Companions. We will explore the textual proof, the scope of the prohibition, and an important exception regarding teaching the Quran word by word.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is reciting Quran, and the ruling is haram for ha'id and junub.
The prohibition applies to both ha'id and nufasa' (postnatal bleeding) similarly.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'The menstruating woman and the one in janabah should not recite anything from the Quran.'
This hadith is ahad, but accepted in Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'shay'an' (anything) in a negative context denotes generality, covering all amounts, even less than an ayat.
An indefinite in the context of negation gives 'umum' (generality) in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars allowed recitation of less than an ayat, but the chosen (mukhtar) view in the Hanafi school is absolute prohibition.
This intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is resolved by the later authorities.
5
Identify the exception
Teaching word by word without the intention of recitation is permissible, as it is not considered qira'ah.
The act of spelling (tahajji) or teaching without recitation intention is exempted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
١٤٣
حنيفة واختلف التصحيح فيما دون الآية وإطلاق المنع هو المختار لقوله : لا تقرأ الحائض ولا الجنب شيئاً من القرآن والنفساء كالحائض (و) يحرم (مسها) أي الآية لقوله تعالى : (لا يمسه إلا المطهرون) سواء كتب على قرطاس أو درهم أو حائط (إلا بغلاف) متجاف عن القرآن والحائل كالخريطة في الصحيح ويكره بالكم تحريماً لتبعيته للابس
المختار كما في البحر والنهر وحيث صحت الرواية عن الإمام فلا يلتفت إلى قول الهندواني لا أفتى بجوازه، وإن روي عن الإمام.
قوله : لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا تقرأ الحائض ولا الجنب شيئاً من القرآن) أي وشيئاً نكرة في سياق النفي فيعم ويؤيده ما أخرجه الدارقطني عن علي رضي الله عنه قال : اقرؤا القرآن ما لم يصب أحدكم جنابة فإذا أصابته فلا ولا حرفاً واحداً والأصح أنه لا بأس بتعليم الحائض والجنب القرآن إذا كان يلقن كلمة كلمة لا على قصد قراءة القرآن كذا في الخلاصة والبزازية أي على قول الكرخي لأنه وإن منع ما دون الآية لكن ما به يسمى قارئاً لا مطلقاً ولهذا قالوا بعدم كراهة التهجي بالقرآن وفي الخانية آخر فصل القراءة تكره قراءة القرآن في مواضع النجاسات كالمغتسل والمخرج والمسلخ وما أشبه ذلك وأما في الحمام إن لم يكن فيه أحد مكشوف العورة وكان الحمام طاهراً فلا بأس بأن يرفع صوته بالقراءة وإن لم يكن كذلك فإن قرأ في نفسه لا يرفع صوته فلا بأس به ولا بأس بالتسبيح والتهليل وإن رفع صوته بذلك، وأما قراءة الماشي، والمحترف إن كان منتبها لا يشغله العمل، والمشي جاز وإلا فلا قال وتكلموا في قراءته مضطجعاً، والأولى أن يقرأ على وجه يكون أقرب إلى التعظيم، ولا بأس بغير القرآن مضطجعاً، والقراءة بالنظر أولى من القراء بالغيب للجمع بين العبادتين.
The book of Purification. 143. Abu Hanifa [differed?] and the correction differed regarding less than an ayah, and the absolute prohibition is the chosen view due to his statement: 'The menstruating woman and the one in janabah should not recite anything from the Quran.' The woman in postnatal bleeding is like the menstruating woman. (And) it is prohibited to touch (it), meaning the ayah, due to Allah's statement: 'None touch it except the purified.' Whether written on paper, a dirham, or a wall. (Except with a covering) that is separate from the Quran, and the barrier is like a pouch according to the sound view, and it is makruh tahriman with the sleeve due to its following the wearer. The chosen view is as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr, and where the narration from the Imam is authentic, no attention is paid to the saying of al-Hinduwani: 'I do not give fatwa permitting it,' even if narrated from the Imam. His statement: 'Due to his saying, peace be upon him: The menstruating woman and the one in janabah should not recite anything from the Quran' - i.e., 'anything' is an indefinite in the context of negation, so it generalizes. And supporting it is what al-Daraqutni narrated from Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: 'Recite the Quran as long as none of you is in janabah; if he becomes so, then not even a single letter.' And the soundest view is that there is no harm in teaching the menstruating woman and the one in janabah the Quran if they are taught word by word without the intention of reciting the Quran. This is as in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya, i.e., according to the saying of al-Karkhi, because although he prohibited less than an ayah, what makes one called a reciter is not absolute. For this reason, they said there is no dislike in spelling out the Quran. In al-Khaniyya, the last chapter on recitation: Reciting the Quran in places of impurities, such as the place of washing, the toilet, the slaughterhouse, and the like, is disliked. As for the bathhouse: if there is no one with exposed awrah and the bathhouse is clean, there is no harm in raising the voice in recitation; if not, then if he recites silently without raising his voice, there is no harm. There is no harm in tasbih and tahlil even if he raises his voice. As for recitation while walking or working: if he is attentive and the work or walking does not distract him, it is permissible; otherwise no. He said: They spoke about his recitation while lying down, and the better is to recite in a manner closest to reverence. There is no harm in reciting other than the Quran while lying down. Recitation by looking is better than recitation by memory because it combines two acts of worship.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the hadith. It establishes that a menstruating woman (ha'id) and a person in the state of major ritual impurity (junub) are prohibited from reciting any part of the Quran, even less than a full ayat. The proof is the hadith: 'The menstruating woman and the one in janabah should not recite anything from the Quran.' The word 'anything' (shay'an) in the context of negation is general, covering all amounts. An additional supporting narration from Ali (RA) explicitly says 'not even a single letter.' The author notes that there is a difference of opinion regarding less than an ayat, but the chosen (mukhtar) view in the Hanafi school is absolute prohibition. However, teaching such individuals by reciting word by word without intending to recite the Quran is permitted, as clarified by al-Karkhi. The passage also discusses other contexts: reciting at places of impurity or in a bathhouse with exposed awrah is disliked, while tasbih and tahlil are always allowed. It concludes that reciting from a written copy (nazar) is superior to reciting from memory because it combines two acts of worship (looking at the Quran and reciting).

Key Terms
الحائض (al-ha'id): A woman experiencing menstrual bleeding.
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
التهجي (al-tahajji): Spelling out the Quran letter by letter without the intention of recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Permissible, as it is not a complete ayat.
B) Disliked (makruh) but not prohibited.
C) Prohibited (haram) absolutely.
D) Permissible only if she is in a state of wudu.

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman or a person in janabah must not recite any part of the Quran, but teaching word by word without recitation intention is permissible.

Prohibition of Touching the Quran and Exceptions
Ruling with proof on touching Quranic writing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching Quranic writing without wudu, identify the Quranic proof, and distinguish between permissible and impermissible barriers (covering vs. sleeve).

Core Idea
Touching the Quran without wudu is haram; a separate covering permits it, but touching with a sleeve is makruh tahriman.

The sanctity of the Quran demands ritual purity for physical contact. This lesson examines the primary proof—the verse 'None touch it except the purified'—and its application to various media (paper, coins, walls) and barriers (detached covering, sleeve). We will also navigate an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the sleeve is a valid barrier.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is touching a Quranic ayah or the Mushaf. The ruling is haram (prohibited) for one without wudu, with an exception for necessity (e.g., fear of burning). The ruling applies whether the ayah is written on paper, a coin, or a wall.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quranic: Surah Al-Waqi'ah 56:79: 'لا يمسه إلا المطهرون'. The verse is decisive in transmission (qati' al-thubut) but its meaning is open to interpretation (zanni al-dalala). The Hanafi school interprets the imperative as a prohibition for others, establishing haram.
3
Analyze the exception: separate covering
Touching the Mushaf through a separate covering (ghilaf mutajafi) such as a pouch is permissible. The barrier must be detached from the Mushaf itself, not attached like a sleeve.
The covering is permissible even if used as a pillow or for riding, provided it is for preservation.
4
Examine the sleeve issue and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Touching the Mushaf with the sleeve of one's garment is disputed. There are two narrations from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: one says it is makruh tahriman (the view chosen by al-Hidayah), the other says it is not disliked because the sleeve is a barrier. The author asserts the chosen view is makruh tahriman due to the sleeve being 'following the wearer' (tābi' li-lābis).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that touching with the sleeve is makruh tahriman. This is strengthened by the fact that the sleeve is not like a separate covering; it is attached to the person, so the prohibition remains, though not as severe as direct touch.
Al-Hidayah and later authorities (al-Bahr, al-Nahr) adopt this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويحرم مسها) أي الآية لقوله تعالى : (لا يمسه إلا المطهرون) سواء كتب على قرطاس أو درهم أو حائط (إلا بغلاف) متجاف عن القرآن والحائل كالخريطة في الصحيح ويكره بالكم تحريماً لتبعيته للابس
المختار كما في البحر والنهر وحيث صحت الرواية عن الإمام فلا يلتفت إلى قول الهندواني لا أفتى بجوازه، وإن روي عن الإمام. قوله: (ويحرم مسها) أي إلا لضرورة كأن يخاف عليه حرقاً أو غرقاً كما في الحموي عن البرجندي، ويحرم ولو كتب بالفارسية إجماعاً لتعلق جواز الصلاة به للعاجز، وكذا سائر الكتب السماوية كما في القهستاني عن الذخيرة نعم ينبغي أن يخص ما لم يبدل منها، وفيما عدا المصحف إنما يحرم مس الكتابة لا الحواشي، ويحرم الكل في المصحف لأن الكل تبع له كما في الحدادي، وغيره وقيد بالآية لأنه يكره مس ما دونها كما في القهستاني، وفي الخانية من بحث القراءة الحربي، أو الذمي إذا طلب تعلم القرآن والفقه والأحكام يعلم رجاء أن يهتدي لكن يمنع من مس المصحف إلا إذا اغتسل، فلا يمنع بعد ذلك قوله : (إلا) بغلاف متجاف) أي متباعد عنهما . قوله : (كالخريطة) وكالخرج الذي فيه المصحف إذا توسده، أو ركب فوقه في السفر يعني إذا كان ذلك لأجل الحفظ وإلا فيكره كما في الخلاصة. قوله: (وبكره بالكم تحريماً) . صححه في الهداية، وفي المحيط وجامع التمرتاشي لا يكره مسه ، بالكم عند العامة لأن المحرم المس، وذلك بالمباشرة باليد بلا حائل وهما روايتان عن محمد كما في النهاية، قوله: التبعيته للابس) ولهذا لا يجوز له أن يفترشه على نجاسة، ويسجد عليه ولا أن يقوم في مصلاه
His statement: 'And it is prohibited to touch it' i.e., the ayah, due to Allah's statement: 'None touch it except the purified.' Whether written on paper, a dirham, or a wall. (Except with a covering) that is separate from the Quran, and the barrier is like a pouch according to the sound view, and it is disliked (makruh tahriman) with the sleeve due to its following the wearer. The chosen view is as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr, and where the narration from the Imam is authentic, no attention is paid to the saying of al-Hinduwani: 'I do not give fatwa permitting it,' even if narrated from the Imam. His statement: ('And it is prohibited to touch it') i.e., except for necessity, such as fear of it being burned or drowned, as in al-Hamawi from al-Birjandi. And it is prohibited even if written in Persian, by consensus, because the permissibility of prayer is attached to it for the incapable. Likewise all other heavenly books, as in al-Qahistani from al-Dhakhira. Yes, it should be specified to the unaltered ones. And other than the Mushaf, only the writing is prohibited to touch, not the margins, but in the Mushaf everything is prohibited because everything is subsidiary to it, as in al-Hadadi and others. And it is restricted to the ayah because touching less than that is disliked (makruh) as in al-Qahistani. In al-Khaniyya from the discussion of recitation: a Harbi or a dhimmi if he asks to learn the Quran, fiqh, and rulings, he is taught in hope that he may be guided, but he is prevented from touching the Mushaf unless he performs ghusl, then he is not prevented afterwards. His statement: '(Except with a covering that is separate)' i.e., distanced from them. His statement: '(like a pouch)' and like the bag containing the Mushaf if he uses it as a pillow or rides upon it during travel, meaning if that is for the sake of preservation; otherwise it is disliked (makruh) as in al-Khulasa. His statement: '(And it is disliked with the sleeve as makruh tahriman).' The author of al-Hidayah deemed it correct (sahhaha), but in al-Muhit and Jami' al-Tamurtashi it is not disliked to touch it with the sleeve in public because the prohibited touch is direct with the hand without a barrier, and these are two narrations from Muhammad as in al-Nihaya. His statement: '(due to its following the wearer)' and for this reason he is not allowed to spread it on impurity, nor prostrate on it, nor stand in his prayer place.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and proof for the prohibition of touching a Quranic ayah (or the Mushaf) by one without wudu. The proof is Quranic: 'None touch it except the purified' (56:79). The ruling covers writing on paper, coins, or walls. An exception is made for necessity (e.g., fear of burning or drowning). The prohibition applies even to Persian translations (by consensus) and other heavenly books (if unaltered). In a full Mushaf, the entire book is sacred; touching the binding or margins is also prohibited because they are subsidiary. However, for other books containing Quranic verses, only the actual writing is prohibited to touch, not the margins. There is a discussion of touching via sleeve: the author (al-Tahtawi) holds it is makruh tahriman due to following the wearer, but there are two narrations from Muhammad al-Shaybani. The stronger view in al-Hidayah is makruh tahriman, while other sources say it is not disliked if done publicly due to general necessity (umum al-balwa). The passage also addresses handling of the Mushaf in travel (e.g., using a pouch) and the rule that one cannot use the Mushaf as a pillow or prostrate on it.

Key Terms
المصحف (al-mushaf): A bound copy of the Quran including its binding and margins.
الغلاف المتجاف (al-ghilaf al-mutajafi): A separate covering that is not attached to the Mushaf, such as a pouch.
بالكم (bil-kumm): Touching the Mushaf while it is inside the sleeve of one's garment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the ruling on touching a Quranic verse written on a wall without wudu?
A) Permissible because the wall is not a Mushaf.
B) Disliked (makruh) but not prohibited.
C) Prohibited (haram) like any other writing of the Quran.
D) Permissible only if touched with a sleeve.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse 'None touch it except the purified' establishes a general prohibition that protects the sanctity of the Quran, with valid exceptions for detached coverings but not for attached sleeves.

Ruling on Entering Mosque During Menstruation and Postnatal Bleeding
Ruling with proof and its refinements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering the mosque for a menstruating woman, a woman with postnatal bleeding, and a person in major impurity (junub), and identify the conditions that permit entry.

Core Idea
Entering the mosque for ha'id, nufasa', and junub is haram, except when necessity makes it unavoidable.

This lesson examines the prohibition of entering the mosque for those in states of ritual impurity that require ghusl. The ruling, based on a prophetic hadith, is clear, but the Hanafi school refines its application by defining exceptions for genuine necessity and addressing specific scenarios such as forgetful entry or becoming junub inside the mosque. Understanding these nuances ensures that the prohibition is observed correctly without undue hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is entering the mosque while in a state of major impurity (haid, nifas, janabah). The basic ruling is haram (prohibited). Note that the ruling includes the Ka'bah but excludes the musalla of Eid and funeral prayers according to the soundest view.
The prohibition applies to the entire mosque building, not just the prayer hall.
2
Recognize the exception for necessity
The prohibition is lifted when there is a genuine necessity (darurah). The classic example given is when the only door of one's house opens directly into the mosque, making it impossible to leave the house without entering the mosque.
Necessity must be genuine and unavoidable; if alternative arrangements can be made, the necessity is not established.
3
Apply the condition for necessity
The necessity must be such that it cannot be circumvented. For example, if the door can be changed or one can live elsewhere, then the necessity is not fulfilled and the prohibition remains.
This strict condition prevents abuse of the exception.
4
Handle the case of becoming junub inside or entering forgetfully
If a person becomes junub inside the mosque, they must perform tayammum and leave immediately if water is unavailable. If they entered forgetfully while junub and then remember, they may leave quickly without tayammum. If they cannot leave, they must perform tayammum and stay, but they may not pray or recite Quran.
The leniency for forgetful entry acknowledges human error.
5
Note the scope of the ruling
The prohibition covers the mosque proper and the Ka'bah, but not the musalla of Eid or funeral prayer grounds, as these are not considered mosques in the same sense.
This distinction is important for practical application during Eid prayer at designated grounds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (دخول) مسجد) شمل الكعبة دون مصلي عيد وجنازة في الأصح، وقيد المنع في الدرر بأن لا يكون ثمة ضرورة فإن كانت كأن يكون باب البيت إلى المسجد، فلا قال في البحر، وينبغي أن يقيد بأن لا يمكن تحويل الباب ولا السكنى في غيره، وإلا لم تتحقق الضرورة، ولو أجنب فيه تيمم، وخرج من ساعته إن لم يقدر على استعمال الماء، وكذا لو دخله وهو جنب ناسياً، ثم ذكر وإن خرج مسرع من غير تيمم جاز وإن لم يقدر على الخروج تيمم، ولبث فيه، ولا يجوز لبثه بدونه إلا أنه لا يصلي ولا يقرأ كما في السراج، وخص من
His statement: '(Entering) a mosque' includes the Ka'bah but excludes the musalla of Eid and funeral prayer according to the soundest view. The prohibition is restricted in al-Durar by the absence of necessity; if there is necessity, such as the door of the house opening into the mosque, then it is not prohibited, as stated in al-Bahr. And it should be conditioned that it is not possible to change the door nor to live elsewhere; otherwise necessity is not realized. If a person becomes junub inside the mosque, he performs tayammum and leaves immediately if he cannot use water. Similarly, if he enters the mosque while being junub forgetfully and then remembers, and he leaves quickly without tayammum, it is permissible. And if he cannot leave, he performs tayammum and stays, and staying without tayammum is not permissible, but he does not pray nor recite, as in al-Siraj. And it is specified from...
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (implied) prohibiting menstruating and postnatal women (and those in janabah) from entering the mosque. The proof is a hadith: 'I do not allow the mosque for the menstruating woman or the junub.' The author clarifies that the ruling includes the Ka'bah but excludes the prayer areas of Eid and funeral prayer (musalla), which are not considered mosques in the same sense. The prohibition is lifted in cases of necessity, e.g., when the only door to the house opens into the mosque. However, the necessity must be genuine—if the door can be changed or one can live elsewhere, the necessity is not established. The passage also addresses the scenario of a person who becomes junub while inside the mosque or enters forgetfully. Such a person must perform tayammum and leave immediately if water is unavailable. If they cannot leave, they may stay after tayammum, but they must not pray or recite Quran while in that state. This aligns with the general rule that a junub cannot remain in the mosque without purification.

Key Terms
المسجد (al-masjid): A mosque or any place designated for congregational prayer; includes the Ka'bah but not the musalla of Eid.
الضرورة (al-darurah): A situation of necessity that permits violating the prohibition, such as having no other entrance to one's home.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a menstruating woman entering the mosque if the only door of her house opens into it?
A) Absolutely prohibited regardless.
B) Permitted due to necessity.
C) Disliked but not prohibited.
D) Permitted only after performing tayammum.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of entering the mosque for ha'id, nufasa', and junub is strict, but genuine necessity lifts it; tayammum facilitates exit or temporary stay.

Concession for Scholars and Ruling on Tafsir Books
Ruling on handling Shariah books and tafsir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi concession for scholars handling Shariah books and explain the exception for tafsir books.

Core Idea
Scholars may handle Quranic books with sleeves, but tafsir requires wudu.

Scholars and students of Shariah have a daily need to handle books containing Quranic verses. Hanafi fiqh provides a special concession for them, distinguishing between books that are primarily Quran and those that are commentary. This lesson examines that concession and its limits, particularly regarding tafsir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its beneficiaries
Read the first part of the passage: who receives the concession and what is the ruling?
The term 'ahl kutub al-shariah' is specific.
2
Understand the reason for the concession
Why did Abu Hanifa grant this concession? What is the legal basis?
Because the Quranic content is subsidiary, not the primary purpose.
3
Note the exception for tafsir
Tafsir is treated differently. What is the ruling for touching tafsir without wudu?
Wudu is required, but some scholars allow it if most of the book is commentary.
4
Compare with the Mushaf
How does the ruling for other books differ from that for the Mushaf?
The Mushaf cannot be touched without wudu at all; other books only the Quranic text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And a concession is given for the people of Shariah books to take them with the sleeve and by hand for necessity, except for tafsir, for which wudu is required to touch it. And it is mustahabb not to take them except with wudu. It is permissible to turn the pages of the Mushaf with something like a pen for recitation. And ordering a boy to carry it and lift it for him is for the necessity of learning. It is not permissible to wrap something in paper on which fiqh or the name of Allah or the Prophet is written. And it is prohibited to erase the name of Allah with saliva, and likewise the Prophet, out of reverence. For the Mushaf, to avoid stepping over it out of modesty and reverence. And the pen shavings and the grass of the mosque should not be thrown in a place of disrespect. (And) it is prohibited for a menstruating woman and one in postnatal bleeding (to enter) a mosque, due to his saying: 'I do not allow the mosque...' And he covers himself quickly, or while wearing shoes over impurity. His statement: 'And a concession is given for the people of Shariah books' is the soundest view according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa) because what is in them of the Quran is in the position of subsidiary. And it is disliked according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as in al-Khulasa. And the restriction to 'the people' indicates its prohibition for others. His statement: 'for necessity' means hardship. His statement: 'except for tafsir' – in al-Ashbah, our companions permitted touching books of tafsir for a person without wudu, and they did not differentiate between whether most of it is tafsir or Quran. And if it were said considering the predominant, it would be good. In al-Jawhara: books of tafsir and others, it is not permissible to touch the places of Quran in them, but he may touch other than that, unlike the Mushaf. I say: that is in accordance with their statements because they made the prohibited in other than the Mushaf the touching of the Quran itself. Some: His statement: 'And it is mustahabb not to take them except with wudu' because they are not free from verses of the Quran. And there is no harm in touching them with the sleeve by agreement due to general necessity (umum al-balwa), as in al-Nihaya from al-Mahbubi. As for writing the Quran, there is no harm if the paper is on the ground according to Abu Yusuf, because he is not carrying the paper; Muhammad disliked that. The scholars of Bukhara. Al-Kamal said: The saying of Abu Yusuf is more analogous because when the paper is on the ground, touching it with a pen is a separate intermediary, so it becomes like a separate pen, unless he touches it with his hand. His statement: '(with saliva)' – consider the ruling if he licks it with his tongue. Taken from him. His statement: '(and likewise the Prophet, al is for the genus, so it includes every prophet, and for this reason he generalized in the sharh.' His statement: '(and he covers the Mushaf)' – apparently it is recommended (nadb). His statement: '(and the pen shavings should not be thrown)' i.e., written with it, as in the sharh. Its apparent meaning is prohibition, unlike new pens. And in it also: when the Mushaf becomes old, not recited from it, and there is fear of it falling, it is placed in a clean cloth and buried in a place that is not trodden upon.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings primarily from the commentary on the text. It discusses concessions for scholars of Shariah: they may handle books containing Quranic verses with sleeves or hands out of necessity, but it is mustahabb to have wudu. The exception is tafsir books, where wudu is required for touching, although some Hanafi scholars allow it without wudu if the Quranic portion is not predominant. It is permissible to turn pages with a pen or similar object. A boy may carry the Mushaf for learning purposes. It is prohibited to use paper with Islamic writing for wrapping. Erasing Allah's name with saliva is prohibited, and the same applies to prophets' names. Regarding the Mushaf, one should not step over it; if it becomes old, it should be wrapped in a clean cloth and buried where not walked on. There is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on writing the Quran while the paper is on the ground: Abu Yusuf permits it, Muhammad dislikes it. Touching tafsir books with the sleeve is unanimously allowed due to general necessity. The passage also reiterates the prohibition of entering the mosque for menstruating and postnatal women.

Key Terms
أهل كتب الشريعة (ahl kutub al-shariah): Scholars and students of Islamic law who have a legitimate need to handle Shariah books.
التفسير (al-tafsir): Quranic exegesis books containing Quranic verses and commentary.
بالكم (bil-kum): With the sleeve of the garment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants a concession to scholars for handling books with Quranic verses, but tafsir requires wudu due to the predominance of Quranic text.

Writing Quran on Ground, Erasing Names, and Mushaf Disposal
Rulings on writing Quran, erasing names, and Mushaf disposal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply Hanafi rulings on writing the Quran on the ground, erasing Allah's name with saliva, and disposing of an old Mushaf.

Core Idea
Writing Quran on the ground is permissible when not carrying the paper; erasing Allah's name with saliva is prohibited; old Mushaf must be buried respectfully.

Besides handling books, fiqh addresses specific acts that may disrespect sacred texts. This lesson covers three distinct rulings: writing Quran on paper placed on the ground, erasing Allah's name with saliva, and the proper disposal of an old, unusable Mushaf. Each has a different level of prohibition and reflects the care required for holy words.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the ruling on writing Quran on the ground
Read the part about writing Quran when the paper is on the ground. What do Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say?
The key is whether the person is 'carrying' the paper.
2
Understand the prohibition of erasing Allah's name
Why is erasing with saliva prohibited? What is the analogy for prophets?
Saliva is considered disrespectful; the rule extends to all prophets.
3
Determine the method of disposing an old Mushaf
When a Mushaf becomes old and unusable, what should be done?
Burial in a clean cloth in a respectful place is the only method mentioned.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi difference
Notice the ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Who follows analogy?
Al-Kamal prefers Abu Yusuf's view as more analogous.

Source Text

And a concession is given for the people of Shariah books to take them with the sleeve and by hand for necessity, except for tafsir, for which wudu is required to touch it. And he covers himself quickly, or while wearing shoes over impurity. His statement: 'And a concession is given for the people of Shariah books' is the soundest view according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa) because what is in them of the Quran is in the position of subsidiary. And it is disliked according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as in al-Khulasa. And the restriction to 'the people' indicates its prohibition for others. His statement: 'for necessity' means hardship. His statement: 'except for tafsir' – in al-Ashbah, our companions permitted touching books of tafsir for a person without wudu, and they did not differentiate between whether most of it is tafsir or Quran. And if it were said considering the predominant, it would be good. In al-Jawhara: books of tafsir and others, it is not permissible to touch the places of Quran in them, but he may touch other than that, unlike the Mushaf. I say: that is in accordance with their statements because they made the prohibited in other than the Mushaf the touching of the Quran itself. Some: His statement: 'And it is mustahabb not to take them except with wudu' because they are not free from verses of the Quran. And there is no harm in touching them with the sleeve by agreement due to general necessity (umum al-balwa), as in al-Nihaya from al-Mahbubi. As for writing the Quran, there is no harm if the paper is on the ground according to Abu Yusuf, because he is not carrying the paper; Muhammad disliked that. The scholars of Bukhara. Al-Kamal said: The saying of Abu Yusuf is more analogous because when the paper is on the ground, touching it with a pen is a separate intermediary, so it becomes like a separate pen, unless he touches it with his hand. His statement: '(with saliva)' – consider the ruling if he licks it with his tongue. Taken from him. His statement: '(and likewise the Prophet, al is for the genus, so it includes every prophet, and for this reason he generalized in the sharh.' His statement: '(and he covers the Mushaf)' – apparently it is recommended (nadb). His statement: '(and the pen shavings should not be thrown)' i.e., written with it, as in the sharh. Its apparent meaning is prohibition, unlike new pens. And in it also: when the Mushaf becomes old, not recited from it, and there is fear of it falling, it is placed in a clean cloth and buried in a place that is not trodden upon.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings primarily from the commentary on the text. It discusses concessions for scholars of Shariah: they may handle books containing Quranic verses with sleeves or hands out of necessity, but it is mustahabb to have wudu. The exception is tafsir books, where wudu is required for touching, although some Hanafi scholars allow it without wudu if the Quranic portion is not predominant. It is permissible to turn pages with a pen or similar object. A boy may carry the Mushaf for learning purposes. It is prohibited to use paper with Islamic writing for wrapping. Erasing Allah's name with saliva is prohibited, and the same applies to prophets' names. Regarding the Mushaf, one should not step over it; if it becomes old, it should be wrapped in a clean cloth and buried where not walked on. There is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on writing the Quran while the paper is on the ground: Abu Yusuf permits it, Muhammad dislikes it. Touching tafsir books with the sleeve is unanimously allowed due to general necessity. The passage also reiterates the prohibition of entering the mosque for menstruating and postnatal women.

Key Terms
الحرقة (al-khirqa): A clean cloth used to wrap the old Mushaf for burial.
البزاق (al-buzaq): Saliva used to erase writing.
براية القلم (barayat al-qalam): Pen shavings (waste from sharpening a pen).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on writing the Quran on a paper placed on the ground, according to the preferred Hanafi view?
A) It is prohibited because it shows disrespect.
B) It is permissible because the writer is not carrying the paper.
C) It is makruh according to all Hanafis.
D) It is permissible only if the writer has wudu.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi fiqh permits writing Quran on paper on the ground if not carried; prohibits erasing Allah's name with saliva; and recommends burying old Mushaf in a clean cloth.

Scholars Exemption for Handling Books of Shariah
Permission for scholars to handle sacred books with necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on scholars touching books of Shariah without wudu and explain the exception for Tafsir.

Core Idea
Scholars may handle books of Shariah without wudu out of necessity, but Tafsir always requires wudu.

This lesson addresses a practical need: scholars who frequently handle books containing Quranic verses. The Hanafi school grants them a license (rukhsah) due to hardship, balancing respect for the Quran with pedagogical necessity. We will examine the ruling, its conditions, and the intra-Hanafi difference of opinion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The passage states that 'people of the books of Shariah' (scholars) are permitted to take such books with the sleeve or hand out of necessity. This is an exemption from the general prohibition of touching the Quran without wudu.
The restriction to 'people' implies prohibition for non-scholars.
2
Note the exception for Tafsir
Tafsir books require wudu for touching, because the Quranic content is substantial and not merely incidental.
Some later Hanafis considered the majority content: if Tafsir predominates, it may be permissible.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa permits scholars to take books without wudu; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it disliked (makruh). The text says Abu Hanifa's view is 'al-ashah' (most correct).
The difference is based on whether the Quran in these books is considered primary or subordinate.
4
Recognize the ruling on touching Tafsir without wudu
Touching Tafsir without wudu is prohibited if it involves direct contact with Quranic verses, but other parts may be touched. This is unlike the Mushaf, where all touch is prohibited.
5
Apply the rule to practical scenarios
A scholar may pick up a fiqh book with his hand for teaching; but if it's a Tafsir book, he should have wudu. Wudu is recommended for all such books.
Touching with a sleeve is universally allowed due to common necessity.

And it is permitted for people of the books of Shariah to take them with the sleeve and by hand out of necessity, except the Tafsir, for touching it requires wudu. And it is recommended not to take them except with wudu. And it is permissible to turn the pages of the Mushaf with something like a pen for reading, and to order a boy to carry it and lift it for the necessity of learning. I say: that is consistent with their words because they made the prohibition in other than the Mushaf touching the essence of the Quran. Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation from the hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah regarding the handling of texts containing Quranic verses and sacred names. The core ruling is that scholars are exempted from the requirement of wudu when taking books of Shariah by sleeve or hand due to necessity, but this is not permissible for others. The permissibility is limited to necessity, akin to hardship. For Tafsir, however, wudu is required when touching it, because it contains Quran. The hashiya notes that Imam Abu Hanifa's view is the most correct, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it disliked. Additionally, it is recommended to handle these books with wudu, but touching with the sleeve is unanimously allowed due to common need. Turning pages of the Mushaf with a pen is allowed for reading, and a child may carry it for learning. Wrapping items in paper containing fiqh or Allah's name is forbidden, as is erasing Allah's name with saliva. Similarly, spitting on the name of a prophet is forbidden. Covering an old Mushaf is recommended, and when it is unusable, it should be wrapped in a clean cloth and buried in a respectful place. The hashiya also discusses the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding writing the Quran on the ground, with Abu Yusuf allowing it based on analogy since the writer does not carry the paper, while Muhammad disliked it. The relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's view according to al-Kamal. The passage emphasizes respect for sacred texts and names, with detailed exceptions for practical needs.

Key Terms
أهل كتب الشريعة (ahl kutub al-shari'ah): People of the books of Shariah: scholars and students of Islamic texts.
التفسير (al-tafsir): Books of Quranic exegesis containing both Quran and commentary.
الضرورة (al-darurah): Necessity or hardship that permits relaxation of normal rules.

Scholars may handle books of Shariah without wudu out of necessity, except for Tafsir which always requires wudu.

Writing Quran on the Ground: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on writing Quran on the ground

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the basis of the intra-Hanafi dispute on writing Quran while the paper is on the ground and identify the mufta bihi opinion.

Core Idea
Writing Quran on the ground is permissible per Abu Yusuf, but disliked by Muhammad due to sanctity.

A practical issue arises when one needs to write Quranic verses on paper that is placed on the ground. Does this disrespect the sacred words? The Hanafi school has a nuanced difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, resolved by al-Kamal in favor of Abu Yusuf on the basis of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
The issue: writing Quran on a paper that is on the ground. Abu Yusuf permits it; Muhammad dislikes it. The text also mentions Mashayikh of Bukhara agreeing with Muhammad.
The difference is not haram vs halal, but makruh vs permissible.
2
Understand Abu Yusuf's proof (qiyas)
Abu Yusuf argues by analogy: touching the Quran with a pen is like writing on a separate piece, because the pen is an intermediary. The writer does not directly carry the paper.
This is a qiyas jaliy: the pen acts as a barrier.
3
Understand Muhammad's proof
Muhammad considers it disliked due to the sanctity (hurmah) of the Quranic words themselves; the act of writing on the ground could be seen as degrading.
His view relies on the concept of hurmah al-Quran.
4
Know the tarjih
Al-Kamal prefers Abu Yusuf's view because it is 'more analogical' (aqyas). The mufta bihi is Abu Yusuf's permissibility.
5
Apply the ruling
Today, if one is writing a verse on a paper placed on a table, the same principle applies: the intermediary (pen) prevents direct contact. Thus, it is permissible but perhaps better to avoid if unnecessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Prohibitions and Etiquettes Regarding Sacred Texts
Prohibitions and etiquettes regarding sacred texts and names

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the prohibited acts concerning sacred names and texts and state the proper method of disposing of an old Mushaf.

Core Idea
Sacred texts and names must be treated with utmost respect; abuse or discarding in disrespectful places is forbidden.

This lesson covers the remaining rulings of the passage: wrapping items in paper that contains sacred names, erasing Allah's name with saliva, and the proper disposal of an old Mushaf. These rules reflect the high regard for the Quran and the names of Allah and the Prophets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited actions
The passage forbids: wrapping something in paper that has fiqh, Allah's name, or the Prophet's name; erasing Allah's name with saliva; and throwing pen shavings or mosque grass in a disrespectful place.
These are acts of disrespect (ihaanah).
2
Understand the ruling on erasing sacred names
Erasing Allah's name with saliva is prohibited because it involves spitting on the name – a clear disrespect. The same applies to the names of all prophets.
The 'al' in 'al-nabi' is for genus, so includes all prophets.
3
Learn the proper disposal of an old Mushaf
When the Mushaf becomes too old to read, it should be wrapped in a clean cloth and buried in a place where it will not be stepped on.
This is a recommended practice, not obligatory, but strongly advised.
4
Note the exception for 'new'
The text says 'unlike the new' regarding throwing pen shavings – meaning that new pen shavings (e.g., from a new pen) may not have the same ruling? The commentary is ambiguous; the apparent meaning is prohibition for used shavings.
This is a minor point; the main ruling is clear.
5
Apply the rulings practically
Today, we must avoid using paper with sacred names for wrapping, and never dispose of such paper in trash. Erasing Allah's name with saliva or licking it is prohibited.
Digital texts also deserve respect, though physical disposal differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويرخص لأهل كتب الشريعة أخذها بالكم وباليد للضرورة إلا التفسير فإنه يجب الوضوء لمسه والمستحب أن لا يأخذها إلا بوضوء ويجوز تقليب أوراق المصحف بنحو قلم للقراءة وأمر الصبي بحمله ورفعه له لضرورة التعلم ولا يجوز لف شيء في كاغد كتب فيه فقه أو اسم الله تعالى، أو النبي ونهي عن محو اسم الله تعالى بالبزاق، ومثله النبي تعظيماً المصحف لوطء زوجته استحياء وتعظيماً، ولا يرمى براية قلم ولا حشيش المسجد في محل ممتهن قوله: (ويرخص لأهل كتب الشريعة) هو الأصح عند الإمام لأن ما فيها من القرآن بمنزلة التابع ويكره عندهما نهر عن الخلاصة، والتقييد بالأهل يؤذن بمنعه لغير الأهل قوله: (للضرورة يعني الحرج. قوله : (إلا) التفسير) في الأشباه، وقد جوز أصحابنا مس كتب التفسير للمحدث، ولم يفصلوا بين كون الأكثر تفسيراً أو قرآناً، ولو قيل به إعتباراً للغالب لكان حسناً وفي الجوهرة كتب التفسير وغيرها لا يجوز مس مواضع القرآن منها، وله أن يمس غيرها بخلاف المصحف . قلت وذلك هو الموافق لكلامهم لأنهم جعلوا المحرم في غير المصحف مس عين القرآن . بعض قوله: (والمستحب أن لا يأخذها إلا بوضوء) لأنها لا تخلو عن آيات القرآن ولا بأس بمسها بالكم إتفاقاً لعموم البلوى كذا في النهاية عن المحبوبي، وأما كتابة القرآن فلا بأس بها إذا كانت الصحيفة على الأرض عند أبي يوسف لأنه ليس بحامل للصحيفة، وكره ذلك محمد مشايخ بخاري. قال الكمال : وقول أبي يوسف أقيس لأنّ الصحيفة إذا كانت على الأرض كان مسها بالقلم وهو واسطة منفصلة فصار كتوب منفصل إلا أن يكو يمسه بيده. قوله : (بالبزاق) انظر حكم ما إذا كان يلعقه بلسانه . أخذ و به قوله: (ومثله النبي أل للجنس فيعم كل نبي، ولذا عممه في الشرح قوله: (ويستر المصحف) الظاهر أنه على وجه الندب قوله: (ولا يرمي براية قلم) أي كتب به كما في الشرح، وظاهره المنع بخلاف الجديد وفيه أيضاً وإذا صار المصحف عتيقاً لا يقرأ فيه، وخيف عليه السقوط يجعل في خرقة طاهرة نظيفة ويدفن في محل لا يوطأ.
And it is permitted for people of the books of Shariah to take them with the sleeve and by hand out of necessity, except the Tafsir, for touching it requires wudu. And it is recommended not to take them except with wudu. And it is permissible to turn the pages of the Mushaf with something like a pen for reading, and to order a boy to carry it and lift it for the necessity of learning. And it is not permissible to wrap anything in paper on which fiqh or the name of Allah, or the Prophet is written. And erasing the name of Allah with saliva is prohibited, and similarly the Prophet, out of respect for the Mushaf, even if one were to step on his wife out of shyness and respect. And one should not throw pen shavings or mosque grass in a place of disrespect. His statement: 'And it is permitted for people of the books of Shariah'—this is the most correct according to Imam Abu Hanifa because what is in them of the Quran is in the position of a follower, and it is disliked according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as in al-Khulasah. And the restriction to 'people' indicates its prohibition for others. His statement: 'out of necessity' meaning hardship. His statement: 'except the Tafsir'—in al-Ashbah, our companions allowed touching Tafsir books for a person in minor impurity, and they did not differentiate between whether the majority is Tafsir or Quran, and if it were said considering the majority it would be good. And in al-Jawharah: Tafsir books and others—it is not permissible to touch the places of Quran from them, and he may touch other than that unlike the Mushaf. I say: that is consistent with their words because they made the prohibition in other than the Mushaf touching the essence of the Quran. Some say: His statement: 'and it is recommended not to take them except with wudu' because they are not free from Quranic verses. And there is no harm in touching them with the sleeve by agreement due to general necessity, as in al-Nihayah from al-Mahbubi. As for writing the Quran, there is no harm if the paper is on the ground according to Abu Yusuf because he is not carrying the paper, and Muhammad disliked that from the Mashayikh of Bukhara. Al-Kamal said: Abu Yusuf's saying is more analogical because when the paper is on the ground, touching it with the pen is a separate intermediary, so it becomes like separate writing unless he touches it with his hand. His statement: 'with saliva'—look at the ruling if he licks it with his tongue. His statement: 'and similarly the Prophet'—the 'al' is for genus, so it includes every prophet, hence he generalized in the commentary. His statement: 'and he covers the Mushaf'—apparently it is recommended. His statement: 'and one should not throw pen shavings'—i.e., what is written with it, as in the commentary, and its apparent meaning is prohibition unlike the new. And also: when the Mushaf becomes old and not readable, and it is feared it may fall, it is placed in a clean pure cloth and buried in a place that is not trodden.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation from the hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah regarding the handling of texts containing Quranic verses and sacred names. The core ruling is that scholars are exempted from the requirement of wudu when taking books of Shariah by sleeve or hand due to necessity, but this is not permissible for others. The permissibility is limited to necessity, akin to hardship. For Tafsir, however, wudu is required when touching it, because it contains Quran. The hashiya notes that Imam Abu Hanifa's view is the most correct, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it disliked. Additionally, it is recommended to handle these books with wudu, but touching with the sleeve is unanimously allowed due to common need. Turning pages of the Mushaf with a pen is allowed for reading, and a child may carry it for learning. Wrapping items in paper containing fiqh or Allah's name is forbidden, as is erasing Allah's name with saliva. Similarly, spitting on the name of a prophet is forbidden. Covering an old Mushaf is recommended, and when it is unusable, it should be wrapped in a clean cloth and buried in a respectful place. The hashiya also discusses the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding writing the Quran on the ground, with Abu Yusuf allowing it based on analogy since the writer does not carry the paper, while Muhammad disliked it. The relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's view according to al-Kamal. The passage emphasizes respect for sacred texts and names, with detailed exceptions for practical needs.

Key Terms
البزاق (al-bizāq): Saliva, especially when used to erase writing.
خرقة طاهرة نظيفة (khirqah tahirah nazifah): A clean, pure cloth used to wrap an old Mushaf before burial.
محل ممتهن (mahall mumtahan): A place of disrespect, e.g., trash, bathroom, or pathway.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Burn it.

C) Wrap it in a clean cloth and bury it in a place not trodden.
D) Recycle it with other paper.

Key Takeaway
Sacred texts and names must be handled with utmost respect; disposal must preserve dignity through burial in clean cloth.

Prohibition of Mosque Entry and Tawaf for Menstruating Women
States prohibition with hadith evidence and clarifies rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mosque entry and tawaf for menstruating women, cite the hadith proof, and explain the concept of shart kamal (condition of perfection).

Core Idea
A menstruating woman is prohibited from mosque entry and tawaf; purity is a condition of perfection, not validity.

In this passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi, we learn the explicit prohibition for menstruating and postpartum women regarding mosques and tawaf. The ruling is based on a clear hadith and further refined by Hanafi usul: purity is not a condition of validity (shart sihha) but a condition of perfection (shart kamal), meaning omission triggers a sacrificial penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: entering the mosque and performing tawaf for a menstruating or postpartum woman. The ruling is haram (prohibited).
The text also mentions that junub (impure by janaba) cannot remain in the mosque, but the focus here is on hayd and nifas.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith: 'I do not allow the mosque for a junub, nor for a menstruating woman' (لا أحل المسجد لجنب ولا حائض). This is a hadith ahad reported by al-Tirmidhi.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala (explicit prohibition indicates haram).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition (nahy) in the hadith indicates tahrim (prohibition) per the usul principle 'al-nahy yufid al-tahrim'. The text also uses analogy: tawaf is like prayer, which requires purity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on the reason for tawaf prohibition
Some might think tawaf is prohibited only because it is in the mosque. Al-Kamal clarifies: the prohibition is intrinsic to tawaf because purity is obligated in it, regardless of location.
This distinction affects rulings on tawaf outside the mosque (e.g., on the roof of the Haram).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that purity is a condition of perfection for tawaf. Therefore, if a menstruating woman performs tawaf al-rukun, her tawaf is considered valid (in the sense of completion) but she must sacrifice a camel.
The same logic applies to a person with minor impurity (hadath): one sheep, unless repeated with purity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يحرم بالحيض والنفاس (دخول مسجد) لقوله : (لا أحل المسجد لجنب، ولا حائض وحكم النفساء كالحائض) (و) يحرم بهما (الطواف) بالكعبة وإن صح لأن الطهارة فيه شرط كمال وتحل به من الإحرام، ويلزمها بدنة في طواف الركن وعلى المحدث شاة إلا أن يعاد على الطهارة لشرف البيت ولأن الطواف به مثل الصلاة كما وردت به السنة (و) يحرم بالحيض والنفاس الجماع والاستمتاع بما تحت السرة إلى تحت الركبة) لقوله تعالى ولا تقربوهن حتى يطهرن، وقوله : «لك ما فوق الإزار فإن وطئها هذا عموم الحكم رسول الله وعلي فيحل لهما المكث بالجنابة لقوله : يا علي لا يحل لأحد يجنب في هذا المسجد غيري وغيرك رواه الترمذي وقال حسن غريب وله طرق متعددة. قوله : ( ويحرمهما (الطواف ولو نفلا . قوله : (لأن الطهارة) أي من الحدثين شرط کمال المعنى إن الصحة لا تتوقف عليها فلا ينافي وجوبها ،له فلا يفوت الجواز بفوتها كما في البرهان، وغيره. قال الكمال : المنظور إليه بالذات في منع الطواف وجوب الطهارة فيه لا كونه في المسجد حتى لو لم يكن ثمة مسجد حرم عليها الطواف أيضاً. قوله: (وعلى المحدث) أي في طواف الركن، وإلا فصدقة . قوله : (إلا أن يعاد على الطهارة أي فلا شيء عليه إذا كانت الإعادة في أيام النحر وإلا وجب دم بتأخيرها عنها قوله لشرف البيت أي لا لكونه في المسجد وهو علة لقوله، ويحرم بهما الطواف . قال العلامة مسكين إنما ذكر الطواف مع أن المنع عن دخول المسجد يغني عنه دفعاً لتوهم أنه لما جاز الوقوف بلا طهارة مع أنه أقوى أركان الج، فلأن يجوز الطواف أولى، أو توهم دخول المسجد لضرورة الطواف، وقد علمت ما قاله الكمال.
(And) it is prohibited for menstruation and postpartum (entering a mosque) because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'I do not allow the mosque for a junub, nor for a menstruating woman' and the ruling for a postpartum woman is like that of a menstruating woman. (And) it is prohibited for them (performing tawaf) around the Kaaba, even if valid, because purity is a condition of perfection, and she becomes free from ihram by it, and a female camel is incumbent upon her in the tawaf of the pillar, and upon a person in minor impurity a sheep, unless he repeats it with purity, due to the honor of the House and because tawaf around it is like prayer as the Sunnah has reported. (And) it is prohibited during menstruation and postpartum (intercourse and enjoyment of what is below the navel to below the knee) because of His statement: 'Do not approach them until they are pure', and his statement (peace be upon him): 'For you is what is above the waist wrapper' and if he has intercourse with her... This is the general ruling. The Messenger of Allah and Ali, so it is permissible for them to stay in a state of janabah because of his statement: 'O Ali, it is not allowed for anyone to be in a state of janabah in this mosque except me and you' narrated by al-Tirmidhi and he said hasan gharib, and it has multiple chains. His statement: 'and it is prohibited for them (tawaf) even if optional.' His statement: 'because purity' i.e., from both major and minor impurities is a condition of perfection, meaning validity does not depend on it, so it does not contradict its obligation, so permissibility is not lost by its absence, as in al-Burhan and others. Al-Kamal said: The primary consideration in prohibiting tawaf is the obligation of purity in it, not because it is in the mosque, so even if there were no mosque, tawaf would still be prohibited for her. His statement: 'and upon the person in minor impurity' i.e., in the tawaf of the pillar, otherwise it is charity. His statement: 'unless he repeats it with purity' i.e., there is no penalty if the repetition occurs during the days of sacrifice, otherwise a blood sacrifice is due for delaying it. His statement: 'due to the honor of the House' i.e., not because it is in the mosque, and this is the cause for his statement: 'and it is prohibited for them tawaf.' Al-Allama Miskin said: He mentioned tawaf even though the prohibition of entering the mosque would suffice, to remove the misunderstanding that since standing at Arafat is allowed without purity even though it is the strongest pillar of Hajj, then tawaf might be more likely to be allowed, or the misunderstanding of entering the mosque for the necessity of tawaf, and you have known what al-Kamal said.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah, addressing the prohibition for menstruating and postpartum women regarding mosque entry and tawaf. The primary evidence is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said he does not allow the mosque for a junub or a menstruating woman. The hashiya clarifies that the prohibition of entering the mosque is general, but there is an exception for the Prophet and Ali as per another hadith. For tawaf, purity is a condition of perfection, so even if a menstruating woman were to perform tawaf, it would be invalid and she must sacrifice a camel if it is the obligatory tawaf (rukn). A person in minor impurity performing tawaf must sacrifice a sheep unless they repeat it with purity. The reason for this strictness is the honor of the Kaaba, and tawaf is likened to prayer. The commentary also addresses potential misunderstandings: one might think that since standing at Arafat is valid without purity, tawaf might also be allowed, but the text clarifies that tawaf requires purity as an obligation not a condition of validity. The hashiya also notes an intra-madhhab point: some scholars differentiate between tawaf being prohibited due to being in the mosque versus due to the act itself; the relied-upon view is that the obligation of purity is intrinsic to tawaf, not merely because it is in the mosque.

Key Terms
الطهارة (al-taharah): Purity from both major and minor impurities (wudu and ghusl).
شرط كمال (shart kamal): A condition of perfection; its absence does not invalidate but may require compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a menstruating woman performs the obligatory tawaf (tawaf al-rukun)?
A) Her tawaf is valid and she must sacrifice a camel.
B) Her tawaf is invalid and she must repeat it after purity.
C) She does not need to do anything because it is not required.
D) She must sacrifice a sheep.

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman is prohibited from tawaf and mosque entry; if she performs the obligatory tawaf, she owes a camel sacrifice because purity is a condition of perfection, not validity.

Prohibition of Sexual Intimacy During Menstruation
States prohibition with Quranic and hadith evidence, and details permitted areas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sexual intimacy during menstruation, identify the Quranic and hadith proofs, and apply the permitted and prohibited zones.

Core Idea
Direct skin contact between navel and knee during menstruation is haram; above navel is permitted.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on marital intimacy during a wife's menstrual period. The Quran and Sunnah establish a clear prohibition of intercourse and any direct contact for pleasure between the navel and knee. Understanding the precise boundaries helps couples observe the limits while maintaining affection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
The text states that enjoyment (al-istimta') of what is below the navel to below the knee is haram. This includes intercourse and direct skin contact for pleasure.
The prohibition is on direct contact, not just intercourse.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The verse 'Do not approach them until they are pure' (2:222) uses the verb 'taqrabu', which Hanafis interpret broadly to include all intimacy, not just intercourse.
The word 'qurb' (approach) is damning in its generality.
3
Locate the hadith proof
The hadith 'For you is what is above the waist wrapper' delineates the permissible area. The izar covers from navel to knee, so above that is allowed.
The hadith implies the area below the izar is prohibited for all intimacy.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Muhammad restricts the prohibited zone to the site of blood only, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf include the entire navel-to-knee area. The fatwa follows the latter.
The text says 'wa bi qawl Muhammad naqul' but then indicates the fatwa is on the broader view.
5
Apply the ruling
Couples may kiss, touch above navel and below knee, but must avoid direct skin contact between navel and knee until the wife performs ghusl after bleeding stops.
Even with a barrier, direct contact for pleasure in the prohibited zone is disliked.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the hashiya on the prohibition of sexual intimacy during menstruation. The Quranic verse 'Do not approach them until they are pure' and the hadith 'For you is what is above the waist wrapper' establish that intercourse and direct skin contact between the navel and knee are haram. The text also clarifies that above the navel and below the knee is permitted. The hashiya then digresses into a discussion about tawaf, likely due to a copy-paste error, but the intended lesson focuses on the prohibition of intimacy. The hashiya notes that the prohibition includes the wife not allowing her husband, and that if she lies about menstruation to prevent intercourse, it is also forbidden. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that the area from navel to knee is prohibited for direct sexual contact during menstruation, but other forms of intimacy are allowed. Some scholars restrict the prohibition to the site of blood flow, but the majority, including the fatwa, includes the entire area between navel and knee.

Key Terms
الإستمتاع (al-istimta'): Sexual enjoyment, including touching and fondling, not limited to intercourse.
الإزار (al-izar): A waist wrapper; in context, it indicates the area that is covered, i.e., below the waist.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits all direct sexual intimacy between navel and knee during menstruation, allowing only above the navel and below the knee, based on Quran and hadith.

Prohibitions During Hayd and Nifas: Intimacy and Tawaf
Rulings on prohibitions for junub, ha'id, and nafsa' with intra-Hanafi dispute on intimacy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibitions during hayd and nifas regarding tawaf and marital intimacy, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the extent of prohibited enjoyment.

Core Idea
Intercourse and direct contact below navel are haram during hayd; but touching with a barrier or above navel is permitted.

Menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas) carry specific prohibitions that affect acts of worship and marital relations. This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi details the prohibitions of tawaf and sexual intimacy, citing Quranic and Prophetic evidence. It also presents an important internal Hanafi debate between Imam Muhammad and the two elders (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) on how much of the body is off-limits for enjoyment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibitions for ha'id and nafsa'
List the acts prohibited during hayd and nifas: staying in the mosque, performing tawaf, and engaging in intercourse or enjoyment of the area below navel to below knee.
The passage also mentions that the prohibition of tawaf is due to the obligation of purification, not the location.
2
Examine the Quranic and Hadith evidence
Locate the primary proof: Quran 2:222 'Do not approach them until they become pure' and the hadith 'For you is what is above the lower garment.' Understand how these texts establish prohibition and permissibility.
The hadith is used by Imam Muhammad to limit the prohibition to the exact locus of blood.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (prohibition of all enjoyment below navel to below knee, even with barrier) with Muhammad's view (prohibition only at the bloodied area). Note that the fatwa is on the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and later al-Ghayah prefers Muhammad's view.
The practical difference: under Muhammad's view, touching thighs with a barrier is permissible.
4
Understand other rulings in the passage
Note additional rules: looking is not prohibited like touching; wife must not lie about menstruation; coitus interruptus is disliked; expiation for intercourse during hayd is a dinar or half dinar.
These are subsidiary but important for comprehensive fiqh knowledge.
